## Δαδδαῖος (id: 001152000000000)

Δαδδαῖος
========

Δαδδαῖος

noun nom

93\.88 · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

\[Glosses \- en] an alternative form of Θαδδαῖος, [93\.150](#93.150) ([MRK 3:18](https://ref.ly/Matt3:18), apparatus)



## δαιμονίζομαι (id: 001153000000000)

δαιμονίζομαι
============

δαιμονίζομαι (G1139)

δαιμόνιον · δαιμονιώδης · δαίμων · δεισιδαιμονία · δεισιδαίμων

12\.41 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

to be demon possessed (derivative of δαιμόνιον\[a] ‘demon,’ [12\.37](#12.37)) to be possessed by a demon In a number of languages one cannot speak of a person ‘being possessed by a demon.’ A more appropriate expression may be ‘the person possesses a demon.’ In other instances an idiomatic phrase is employed, ‘the demon rides the person’ or ‘the demon commands the person’ or even ‘the demon is the person.’

[MAT 4:24](https://ref.ly/Matt4:24) · [MAT 8:16](https://ref.ly/Matt8:16) · [MAT 8:28](https://ref.ly/Matt8:28) · [MAT 8:33](https://ref.ly/Matt8:33) · [MAT 9:32](https://ref.ly/Matt9:32) · [MAT 12:22](https://ref.ly/Matt12:22) · [MAT 15:22](https://ref.ly/Matt15:22) · [MRK 1:32](https://ref.ly/Matt1:32) · [MRK 5:15](https://ref.ly/Matt5:15) · [MRK 5:16](https://ref.ly/Matt5:16) · [MRK 5:18](https://ref.ly/Matt5:18) · [LUK 8:36](https://ref.ly/Mark8:36) · [JHN 10:21](https://ref.ly/Luke10:21)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 4:24; Matthew 8:16; Matthew 8:28; Matthew 8:33; Matthew 9:32; Matthew 12:22; Matthew 15:22; Mark 1:32; Mark 5:15; Mark 5:16; Mark 5:18; Luke 8:36; John 10:21


## δαιμόνιον (id: 001154000000000)

δαιμόνιον
=========

δαιμόνιον (G1140)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 δαιμονίζομαι

12\.37 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

demon, evil spirit an evil supernatural being or spirit While in a number of languages the Devil may be spoken of as ‘the chief of the demons,’ sometimes the demons are simply called ‘the spirits of the Devil’ or ‘the servants of the Devil.’  
In a number of languages the difficulty in terminology for demons is not the absence of a term, but the abundance of different terms for different kinds of demons, each one of which may be responsible for particular kinds of human behavior, for example, insanity, depression, epilepsy, sex perversion, and violent assault. Sometimes demons are classified as ‘those of the home’ and ‘those of the forest,’ in which case the latter are normally regarded as more violent and virulent. When there is an abundance of different terms for demons and no generic term for all types of demons, one can usually select a class of demons which parallels most closely the descriptions of demon activity in the NT and use such a term with appropriate contextual qualifications so as to suggest that such a term is to be understood in a general sense.

[MAT 7:22](https://ref.ly/Matt7:22) · [MAT 9:33](https://ref.ly/Matt9:33) · [MAT 9:34](https://ref.ly/Matt9:34) · [MAT 9:34](https://ref.ly/Matt9:34) · [MAT 10:8](https://ref.ly/Matt10:8) · [MAT 11:18](https://ref.ly/Matt11:18) · [MAT 12:24](https://ref.ly/Matt12:24) · [MAT 12:24](https://ref.ly/Matt12:24) · [MAT 12:27](https://ref.ly/Matt12:27) · [MAT 12:28](https://ref.ly/Matt12:28) · [MAT 17:18](https://ref.ly/Matt17:18) · [MRK 1:34](https://ref.ly/Matt1:34) · [MRK 1:34](https://ref.ly/Matt1:34) · [MRK 1:39](https://ref.ly/Matt1:39) · [MRK 3:15](https://ref.ly/Matt3:15) · [MRK 3:22](https://ref.ly/Matt3:22) · [MRK 3:22](https://ref.ly/Matt3:22) · [MRK 6:13](https://ref.ly/Matt6:13) · [MRK 7:26](https://ref.ly/Matt7:26) · [MRK 7:29](https://ref.ly/Matt7:29) · [MRK 7:30](https://ref.ly/Matt7:30) · [MRK 9:38](https://ref.ly/Matt9:38) · [MRK 16:9](https://ref.ly/Matt16:9) · [MRK 16:17](https://ref.ly/Matt16:17) · [LUK 4:33](https://ref.ly/Mark4:33) · [LUK 4:35](https://ref.ly/Mark4:35) · [LUK 4:41](https://ref.ly/Mark4:41) · [LUK 7:33](https://ref.ly/Mark7:33) · [LUK 8:2](https://ref.ly/Mark8:2) · [LUK 8:27](https://ref.ly/Mark8:27) · [LUK 8:29](https://ref.ly/Mark8:29) · [LUK 8:30](https://ref.ly/Mark8:30) · [LUK 8:33](https://ref.ly/Mark8:33) · [LUK 8:35](https://ref.ly/Mark8:35) · [LUK 8:38](https://ref.ly/Mark8:38) · [LUK 9:1](https://ref.ly/Mark9:1) · [LUK 9:42](https://ref.ly/Mark9:42) · [LUK 9:49](https://ref.ly/Mark9:49) · [LUK 10:17](https://ref.ly/Mark10:17) · [LUK 11:14](https://ref.ly/Mark11:14) · [LUK 11:20](https://ref.ly/Mark11:20) · [LUK 13:32](https://ref.ly/Mark13:32) · [JHN 7:20](https://ref.ly/Luke7:20) · [JHN 8:48](https://ref.ly/Luke8:48) · [JHN 8:49](https://ref.ly/Luke8:49) · [JHN 8:52](https://ref.ly/Luke8:52) · [JHN 10:20](https://ref.ly/Luke10:20) · [JHN 10:21](https://ref.ly/Luke10:21) · [1CO 10:20](https://ref.ly/Rom10:20) · [1CO 10:20](https://ref.ly/Rom10:20) · [1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21) · [1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21) · [1TI 4:1](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:1) · [JAS 2:19](https://ref.ly/Heb2:19) · [REV 9:20](https://ref.ly/Jude9:20) · [REV 16:14](https://ref.ly/Jude16:14) · [REV 18:2](https://ref.ly/Jude18:2)

12\.26 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

god, lesser god a supernatural being of somewhat lesser status than θεός\[b] ‘god’ ([12\.22](#12.22)) The expression ‘foreign gods’ ([ACT 17:18](https://ref.ly/John17:18)) may be rendered as ‘gods whom the foreigners worshiped’ or ‘gods of the foreigners.’ It would be wrong to render ‘foreign gods’ by a phrase which would mean ‘the gods are foreigners.’

[ACT 17:18](https://ref.ly/John17:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 7:22; Matthew 9:33; Matthew 9:34; Matthew 10:8; Matthew 11:18; Matthew 12:24; Matthew 12:27; Matthew 12:28; Matthew 17:18; Mark 1:34; Mark 1:39; Mark 3:15; Mark 3:22; Mark 6:13; Mark 7:26; Mark 7:29; Mark 7:30; Mark 9:38; Mark 16:9; Mark 16:17; Luke 4:33; Luke 4:35; Luke 4:41; Luke 7:33; Luke 8:2; Luke 8:27; Luke 8:29; Luke 8:30; Luke 8:33; Luke 8:35; Luke 8:38; Luke 9:1; Luke 9:42; Luke 9:49; Luke 10:17; Luke 11:14; Luke 11:15; Luke 11:18; Luke 11:19; Luke 11:20; Luke 13:32; John 7:20; John 8:48; John 8:49; John 8:52; John 10:20; John 10:21; 1 Corinthians 10:20; 1 Corinthians 10:21; 1 Timothy 4:1; James 2:19; Revelation 9:20; Revelation 16:14; Revelation 18:2; Acts 17:18


## δαιμονιώδης (id: 001155000000000)

δαιμονιώδης
===========

δαιμονιώδης (G1141)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ες 

|  |
| --- |

 δαιμονίζομαι

12\.40 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

demonic, devilish (derivative of δαιμόνιον\[a] ‘demon,’ [12\.37](#12.37)) pertaining to a demon In some languages δαιμονιώδης may be rendered as ‘typical of the way a demon acts’ or ‘the way in which demons behave.’

[JAS 3:15](https://ref.ly/Heb3:15)

* **Associated Passages:** James 3:15


## δαίμων (id: 001156000000000)

δαίμων
======

δαίμων (G1142)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ονος 

|  |
| --- |

 δαιμονίζομαι

12\.37 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

demon, evil spirit an evil supernatural being or spirit While in a number of languages the Devil may be spoken of as ‘the chief of the demons,’ sometimes the demons are simply called ‘the spirits of the Devil’ or ‘the servants of the Devil.’  
In a number of languages the difficulty in terminology for demons is not the absence of a term, but the abundance of different terms for different kinds of demons, each one of which may be responsible for particular kinds of human behavior, for example, insanity, depression, epilepsy, sex perversion, and violent assault. Sometimes demons are classified as ‘those of the home’ and ‘those of the forest,’ in which case the latter are normally regarded as more violent and virulent. When there is an abundance of different terms for demons and no generic term for all types of demons, one can usually select a class of demons which parallels most closely the descriptions of demon activity in the NT and use such a term with appropriate contextual qualifications so as to suggest that such a term is to be understood in a general sense.

[MAT 8:31](https://ref.ly/Matt8:31)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:31

[LUK 7:38](https://ref.ly/Mark7:38) · [LUK 7:44](https://ref.ly/Mark7:44) · [ACT 20:19](https://ref.ly/John20:19) · [ACT 20:31](https://ref.ly/John20:31) · [2CO 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:4) · [2TI 1:4](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:4) · [HEB 5:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:7) · [HEB 12:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:17) · [REV 7:17](https://ref.ly/Jude7:17) · [REV 21:4](https://ref.ly/Jude21:4)

## δακρύω (id: 001159000000000)

δακρύω
======

δακρύω (G1145)

δάκρυον

25\.137 · Attitudes and Emotions · Laugh, Cry, Groan

to weep, to cry to weep, with the clear implication of shedding tears In a number of languages a clear distinction is made between weeping which results from sorrow and grief and weeping caused by physical suffering. Without careful attention to such a distinction, a translator may seriously distort the meaning of the text.

[JHN 11:35](https://ref.ly/Luke11:35)

* **Associated Passages:** John 11:35


## δακτύλιος (id: 001160000000000)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 δείκνυμι

6\.190 · Artifacts · Adornments

ring a ring for the finger, normally made of gold or silver and usually containing the signet of the owner by which he could mark ownership and seal documents

[LUK 15:22](https://ref.ly/Mark15:22)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 15:22


## δάκτυλος (id: 001161000000000)

δάκτυλος
========

δάκτυλος (G1147)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 δείκνυμι

8\.34 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

finger one of the five long and slender projections of the human hand, used for writing, pointing, grasping, and other activities Though it may seem quite logical to speak of ‘writing with the finger’ ([JHN 8:6](https://ref.ly/Luke8:6)), in some languages one is required to speak of ‘writing with the hand.’ Similarly, in [MAT 23:4](https://ref.ly/Matt23:4) the idiom ‘to lift a finger’ is more satisfactorily expressed as ‘to lift a hand.’ Expressions such as ‘to lift the hand’ and ‘to lift the finger’ must be carefully studied for their idiomatic significance, for ‘to lift the hand’ may mean ‘to release something,’ while ‘to lift the finger’ may be a lewd gesture.  
In a number of languages the expression ‘to lift a finger’ ([MAT 23:4](https://ref.ly/Matt23:4)) may be best rendered as ‘to do a thing to help’ or ‘to help in any way.’ For δάκτυλος θεοῦ ‘the finger of God’ ([LUK 11:20](https://ref.ly/Mark11:20)), see [76\.3](#76.3).

[MAT 23:4](https://ref.ly/Matt23:4) · [MRK 7:33](https://ref.ly/Matt7:33) · [LUK 11:46](https://ref.ly/Mark11:46) · [LUK 16:24](https://ref.ly/Mark16:24) · [JHN 8:6](https://ref.ly/Luke8:6) · [JHN 20:25](https://ref.ly/Luke20:25) · [JHN 20:27](https://ref.ly/Luke20:27)

76\.3 · Power, Force

power power as an expression of the activity of a person or supernatural being1 In some languages there is no abstract term for ‘power.’ The equivalent of doing something by the power of someone is ‘someone makes it possible to do’ or, in a figurative sense, ‘someone gives strength to do.’

[LUK 11:20](https://ref.ly/Mark11:20)

1 It is possible that χείρ\[c], βραχίων, and δάκτυλος\[b] in the figurative sense of power of an individual differ somewhat in meaning one from the other, but it is impossible to determine this on the basis of existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 23:4; Mark 7:33; Luke 11:46; Luke 16:24; John 8:6; John 20:25; John 20:27; Luke 11:20

## δαμάζω (id: 001164000000000)

δαμάζω
======

δαμάζω (G1150)

δαμάω (tame) · δάμαλις

37\.1 · Control, Rule · Control, Restrain

to control, to bring under control, to hold in check to bring under control and to continue to restrain In many languages it may be difficult to speak of ‘bringing a person under control.’ It may therefore be more appropriate to use some such phrase as ‘not allow a person to do just what he wants’ or ‘make a person behave’ or ‘make a person obey.’ In speaking of animals, one may render [JAS 3:7](https://ref.ly/Heb3:7) as ‘all kinds of wild animals ... can be made to obey a person.’

[MRK 5:4](https://ref.ly/Matt5:4) · [JAS 3:7](https://ref.ly/Heb3:7) · [JAS 3:7](https://ref.ly/Heb3:7) · [JAS 3:8](https://ref.ly/Heb3:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 5:4; James 3:7; James 3:8

=======

δάμαλις (G1151)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-εως 

|  |
| --- |

 δαμάζω

4\.18 · Animals · Animals

heifer the young female of cattle A δάμαλις ‘heifer’ would be older and bigger than a calf but younger than a cow, since ‘heifer’ refers to a cow before she has been impregnated or given birth to her first calf.

[HEB 9:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 9:13

## δανίζω (id: 001170000000000)

δανίζω
======

δανίζω (G1155a) — δανείζω, δανείζομαι

aor.subj. δανίσω 

|  |
| --- |

 δάνειον · δανιστής

57\.209 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Lend, Loan, Interest, Borrow, Bank

to make a loan, to lend money to lend money, normally with the expectation of receiving the same amount in return plus interest In [LUK 6:34](https://ref.ly/Mark6:34) it is possible that no interest payment is involved, in which case the meaning is similar to that of κίχρημι ‘to lend’ ([57\.214](#57.214)).

[LUK 6:34](https://ref.ly/Mark6:34) · [LUK 6:34](https://ref.ly/Mark6:34) · [LUK 6:35](https://ref.ly/Mark6:35)

57\.213 · (δανείζομαι) · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Lend, Loan, Interest, Borrow, Bank

to borrow money to borrow money, normally with the implication of interest to be paid It is possible, however, that in [MAT 5:42](https://ref.ly/Matt5:42) interest on the loan is not involved.

[MAT 5:42](https://ref.ly/Matt5:42)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 6:34; Luke 6:35; Matthew 5:42

## δαπανάω (id: 001173000000000)

δαπανάω
=======

δαπανάω (G1159)

ἀδάπανος · δαπάνη · ἐκδαπανάομαι · προσδαπανάω

57\.146 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Spend, Waste

to spend, to pay out, to pay expenses to pay out money (or other assets) as a means of obtaining benefits or in payment for benefits For another interpretation of δαπανάω in [2CO 12:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:15), see δαπανάω\[c] [42\.27](#42.27).

[MRK 5:26](https://ref.ly/Matt5:26) · [LUK 15:14](https://ref.ly/Mark15:14) · [ACT 21:24](https://ref.ly/John21:24) · [2CO 12:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:15)

57\.149 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Spend, Waste

to spend completely, to waste to spend completely, with the implication of uselessly, and therefore, to waste In some languages ‘to waste’ may be expressed as ‘to use up and to get no benefit’ or ‘to have, but for no purpose.’

[JAS 4:3](https://ref.ly/Heb4:3)

42\.27 · Perform, Do · Do, Perform

to do anything, to exert great effort (a figurative extension of meaning of δαπανάω\[a] ‘‘to spend,’ [57\.146](#57.146)) to exert great effort in doing something It is possible, however, that δαπανάω in [2CO 12:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:15) should be understood in the literal sense and hence rendered ‘I will be glad to spend all I have on your behalf’ (see δαπανάω\[a] [57\.146](#57.146)).

[2CO 12:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 5:26; Luke 15:14; Acts 21:24; 2 Corinthians 12:15; James 4:3

## δέ (id: 001176000000000)

δέ
==

δέ (G1161)

cj

89\.94 · Relations · Addition

and a marker of an additive relation, but with the possible implication of some contrast

89\.104 · Relations · Addition

**Collocation:** μέν ... δέ

some ... others, first ... then a marker of two or more items which are additively related and thematically parallel

89\.136 · Relations · Contrast

**Collocation:** μέν ... δέ

on the one hand ... but on the other hand a marker of sets of items in contrast with one another

## δέησις (id: 001177000000000)

δέησις
======

δέησις (G1162)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-εως 

|  |
| --- |

 δέομαι

33\.171 · Communication · Ask For, Request

request, plea, prayer (derivative of δέομαι ‘to plead, to beg,’ [33\.170](#33.170)) that which is asked with urgency based on presumed need1

[LUK 1:13](https://ref.ly/Mark1:13) · [LUK 2:37](https://ref.ly/Mark2:37) · [LUK 5:33](https://ref.ly/Mark5:33) · [ROM 10:1](https://ref.ly/Acts10:1) · [2CO 1:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:11) · [2CO 9:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:14) · [EPH 6:18](https://ref.ly/Gal6:18) · [EPH 6:18](https://ref.ly/Gal6:18) · [PHP 1:4](https://ref.ly/Eph1:4) · [PHP 1:4](https://ref.ly/Eph1:4) · [PHP 1:19](https://ref.ly/Eph1:19) · [PHP 4:6](https://ref.ly/Eph4:6) · [1TI 2:1](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:1) · [1TI 5:5](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:5) · [2TI 1:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:3) · [HEB 5:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:7) · [JAS 5:16](https://ref.ly/Heb5:16) · [1PE 3:12](https://ref.ly/Jas3:12)

1 Though δέησις basically means ‘that which is asked for urgently,’ in the NT it occurs only in connection with pleas made to God, and therefore it is properly translated as ‘prayer.’

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:13; Luke 2:37; Luke 5:33; Romans 10:1; 2 Corinthians 1:11; 2 Corinthians 9:14; Ephesians 6:18; Philippians 1:4; Philippians 1:19; Philippians 4:6; 1 Timothy 2:1; 1 Timothy 5:5; 2 Timothy 1:3; Hebrews 5:7; James 5:16; 1 Peter 3:12


## δεῖ (id: 001178000000000)

δεῖ
===

δεῖ (G1163)

subj. δέῃ · inf. δεῖν · ptc. δέον · impf. ἔδει 

|  |
| --- |

 δέω

71\.34 · Mode · Necessary, Unnecessary

to be necessary, must to be that which must necessarily take place, often with the implication of inevitability It is impossible to tell in a context such as [MRK 13:7](https://ref.ly/Matt13:7) whether δεῖ implies mere inevitability of an event or whether the events are somehow part of the plan and purpose of God. The latter interpretation could only be derived from broader theological implications and not from the meaning of δεῖ itself.

## δεῖγμα (id: 001179000000000)

δεῖγμα
======

δεῖγμα (G1164)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-τος 

|  |
| --- |

 δείκνυμι

28\.48 · Know · Well Known, Clearly Shown, Revealed

example (such as to warn), means by which something is known (derivative of δείκνυμι\[a] ‘to make known,’ [28\.47](#28.47)) the means by which the nature of something is made known, particularly as an example of what is to be avoided

[JUD 1:7](https://ref.ly/3John1:7)

* **Associated Passages:** Jude 1:7

δειγματίζω (G1165)

δείκνυμι

25\.200 · Attitudes and Emotions · Shame, Disgrace, Humiliation

to disgrace in public, to put to shame to cause someone to suffer public disgrace or shame The expression ‘to disgrace in public’ may be rendered in some languages as ‘to cause everyone to think bad about’ or ‘to cause everyone to speak in whispers about.’

[MAT 1:19](https://ref.ly/Matt1:19) · [COL 2:15](https://ref.ly/Phil2:15)

## δείκνυμι (id: 001181000000000)

δείκνυμι
========

δείκνυμι (G1166a)

fut. δείξω · aor. ἔδειξα · impv. δεῖξον · aor.pass.ptc. δειχθείς 

|  |
| --- |

 ἀναδείκνυμι · ἀνάδειξις · ἀποδείκνυμι · ἀπόδειξις · δακτύλιος · δάκτυλος · δεῖγμα · δειγματίζω · ἔνδειγμα · ἐνδείκνυμι · ἔνδειξις · ἐπιδείκνυμι · παραδειγματίζω · ὑπόδειγμα · ὑποδείκνυμι · χρυσοδακτύλιος

28\.47 · Know · Well Known, Clearly Shown, Revealed

to make known, to demonstrate, to show to make known the character or significance of something by visual, auditory, gestural, or linguistic means1 For another interpretation of δείκνυμι in [1CO 12:31](https://ref.ly/Rom12:31), see δείκνυμι\[b] [33\.150](#33.150).

[MAT 4:8](https://ref.ly/Matt4:8) · [MAT 8:4](https://ref.ly/Matt8:4) · [MRK 1:44](https://ref.ly/Matt1:44) · [MRK 14:15](https://ref.ly/Matt14:15) · [LUK 4:5](https://ref.ly/Mark4:5) · [LUK 5:14](https://ref.ly/Mark5:14) · [LUK 20:24](https://ref.ly/Mark20:24) · [LUK 22:12](https://ref.ly/Mark22:12) · [LUK 24:40](https://ref.ly/Mark24:40) · [JHN 2:18](https://ref.ly/Luke2:18) · [JHN 5:20](https://ref.ly/Luke5:20) · [JHN 5:20](https://ref.ly/Luke5:20) · [JHN 10:32](https://ref.ly/Luke10:32) · [JHN 14:8](https://ref.ly/Luke14:8) · [JHN 14:9](https://ref.ly/Luke14:9) · [JHN 20:20](https://ref.ly/Luke20:20) · [ACT 7:3](https://ref.ly/John7:3) · [ACT 10:28](https://ref.ly/John10:28) · [1CO 12:31](https://ref.ly/Rom12:31)3 · [1TI 6:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:15) · [JAS 2:18](https://ref.ly/Heb2:18) · [JAS 2:18](https://ref.ly/Heb2:18) · [JAS 3:13](https://ref.ly/Heb3:13) · [REV 1:1](https://ref.ly/Jude1:1) · [REV 4:1](https://ref.ly/Jude4:1) · [REV 17:1](https://ref.ly/Jude17:1) · [REV 21:9](https://ref.ly/Jude21:9) · [REV 21:10](https://ref.ly/Jude21:10) · [REV 22:1](https://ref.ly/Jude22:1) · [REV 22:6](https://ref.ly/Jude22:6) · [REV 22:8](https://ref.ly/Jude22:8)

33\.150 · Communication · Interpret, Mean, Explain

to show, to explain, to make clear to explain the meaning or significance of something by demonstration2 For another interpretation of δείκνυμι in [1CO 12:31](https://ref.ly/Rom12:31), see δείκνυμι\[a] [28\.47](#28.47).

[MAT 16:21](https://ref.ly/Matt16:21) · [1CO 12:31](https://ref.ly/Rom12:31)3 · [HEB 8:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:5)

1 It is possible that ὑποδείκνυμι\[a] is somewhat more emphatic or intensive in connotation than δείκνυμι\[a], but this cannot be shown from existing contexts. 2 There may very well be a slight difference of meaning between δείκνυμι\[b] and ὑποδείκνυμι\[b], but this cannot be determined from existing contexts. 3 1CO 12:31 The ‘more excellent way’ referred to in [1CO 12:31](https://ref.ly/Rom12:31) consists of a verbal statement occurring in 1 Cor 13, so that in this context δείκνυμι refers to an oral communication, but the content of 1 Cor 13 involves far more than oral communication, so that in the context of [1CO 12:31](https://ref.ly/Rom12:31), one is perfectly justified in analyzing the meaning as being essentially ‘causing to know.’ It is obviously very difficult to determine in the case of δείκνυμι\[b] and ὑποδείκνυμι\[b] whether the focus is upon the act of communication or upon the resulting knowledge or understanding of the receptors. The same type of difficulty occurs in the meanings listed in [33\.151](#33.151)\-[33\.154](#33.154).

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 4:8; Matthew 8:4; Mark 1:44; Mark 14:15; Luke 4:5; Luke 5:14; Luke 20:24; Luke 22:12; Luke 24:40; John 2:18; John 5:20; John 10:32; John 14:8; John 14:9; John 20:20; Acts 7:3; Acts 10:28; 1 Corinthians 12:31; 1 Timothy 6:15; James 2:18; James 3:13; Revelation 1:1; Revelation 4:1; Revelation 17:1; Revelation 21:9; Revelation 21:10; Revelation 22:1; Revelation 22:6; Revelation 22:8; Matthew 16:21; Hebrews 8:5


## δειλία (id: 001182000000000)

δειλία

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ας 

|  |
| --- |

 δειλιάω

25\.266 · Attitudes and Emotions · Fear, Terror, Alarm

cowardice, timidity a state of fear because of a lack of courage or moral strength ‘Cowardice’ is often rendered by means of an idiom, for example, ‘to have a fallen heart,’ ‘to have a soft heart,’ or ‘one’s heart has disappeared.’

[2TI 1:7](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:7)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Timothy 1:7

## δεῖνα (id: 001185000000000)

δεῖνα
=====

δεῖνα (G1170)

noun

92\.19 · Discourse Referentials · Whom or What Spoken or Written About

certain, somebody a reference to an entity which one cannot or does not wish to make explicit (in the NT only a reference to a man) Though in many translations δεῖνα is translated as ‘certain,’ this can give a wrong impression since it would imply that the individual is known to the parties involved or has been identified by the context.

[MAT 26:18](https://ref.ly/Matt26:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 26:18


## δεινός (id: 001186000000000)

δεινός
======

δεινός

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ή, \-όν 

|  |
| --- |

 δειλιάω

22\.31 · Trouble, Hardship, Relief, Favorable Circumstances · Difficult, Hard

difficult, hard, severe pertaining to that which is severe or hard, with the implication of fear This word is found as a variant reading only: ἀλλὰ ἐγγίζει ἄλλα δεινά ‘but other severe (afflictions) are near’ [MRK 16:14](https://ref.ly/Matt16:14) (apparatus).

## δειπνέω (id: 001188000000000)

23\.20 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

## δεῖπνον (id: 001189000000000)

δεῖπνον
=======

δεῖπνον (G1173)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 δειπνέω

23\.22 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

a meal, a banquet, a feast a meal whether simple or elaborate (this generic meaning of δεῖπνον is in contrast with the more specific meaning of δεῖπνον\[b], [23\.25](#23.25)) Though ἄριστον\[a], δεῖπνον\[a], and βρῶσις\[b] are highly generic in this usage, it is not necessary to translate these terms by a corresponding generic term in another language, since a more specific term may fit the context more satisfactorily. In fact, a generic term might be quite inappropriate in that it would suggest in the case of [MRK 6:21](https://ref.ly/Matt6:21) that Herod was quite stingy in simply providing an ordinary meal for his officials.

[MRK 6:21](https://ref.ly/Matt6:21) · [MRK 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39) · [1CO 11:20](https://ref.ly/Rom11:20) · [1CO 11:21](https://ref.ly/Rom11:21)

23\.25 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

supper, main meal the principal meal of the day, usually in the evening Though in the so\-called Western world there is a tendency to have three meals each day, breakfast, lunch, and dinner (or supper), in many parts of the world there are only two principal meals: one eaten around nine or ten o’clock in the morning, and another at four or five o’clock in the afternoon.  
In some languages there is a very important distinction made between a more or less formal meal and the relatively informal times of eating which might be called ‘snacks.’ These would be occasions on which one would eat only one kind of food and possibly in relatively small quantities.

[MAT 23:6](https://ref.ly/Matt23:6) · [LUK 14:12](https://ref.ly/Mark14:12) · [LUK 14:16](https://ref.ly/Mark14:16) · [LUK 14:17](https://ref.ly/Mark14:17) · [LUK 14:24](https://ref.ly/Mark14:24) · [LUK 20:46](https://ref.ly/Mark20:46) · [JHN 12:2](https://ref.ly/Luke12:2) · [JHN 13:2](https://ref.ly/Luke13:2) · [JHN 13:4](https://ref.ly/Luke13:4) · [JHN 21:20](https://ref.ly/Luke21:20)

94\.7

feast, banquet an elaborate meal

[MAT 23:6](https://ref.ly/Matt23:6) · [MRK 6:21](https://ref.ly/Matt6:21) · [MRK 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39) · [LUK 14:12](https://ref.ly/Mark14:12) · [LUK 14:16](https://ref.ly/Mark14:16) · [LUK 14:17](https://ref.ly/Mark14:17) · [LUK 14:24](https://ref.ly/Mark14:24) · [LUK 20:46](https://ref.ly/Mark20:46) · [REV 19:9](https://ref.ly/Jude19:9) · [REV 19:17](https://ref.ly/Jude19:17)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 6:21; Mark 12:39; 1 Corinthians 11:20; 1 Corinthians 11:21; Matthew 23:6; Luke 14:12; Luke 14:16; Luke 14:17; Luke 14:24; Luke 20:46; John 12:2; John 13:2; John 13:4; John 21:20; Revelation 19:9; Revelation 19:17

## δεισιδαίμων (id: 001191000000000)

δεισιδαίμων
===========

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ον, \-ονος 

|  |
| --- |

 δεισιδαιμονία

53\.3 · Religious Activities · Religious Practice

religious pertaining to being religious δεισιδαίμων may occur in either a good or a bad sense; that is to say, it may mean either ‘very religious’ or ‘superstitious,’ although the meaning of ‘superstitious’ is primarily a later development in the meaning of this word. In [ACT 17:22](https://ref.ly/John17:22) there seems every reason to believe that Paul was using the term in a positive sense.

[ACT 17:22](https://ref.ly/John17:22)

## δεκατέσσαρες (id: 001196000000000)

δεκατέσσαρες
============

δεκατέσσαρες (G1180)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 δέκα \+ τέσσαρες

60\.22 · Number · One, Two, Three, Etc. \[Cardinals]

fourteen cardinal number, where there are fourteen instances of a countable entity It is possible that δεκατέσσαρες in [MAT 1:17](https://ref.ly/Matt1:17) has a symbolic meaning in view of its being equivalent to twice seven. Others have suggested that the number fourteen is derived from the value of the name David based on the numerical values of the consonants in the Hebrew form of the name. This may explain certain of the irregularities in the listing of the generations.

[MAT 1:17](https://ref.ly/Matt1:17) · [MAT 1:17](https://ref.ly/Matt1:17) · [MAT 1:17](https://ref.ly/Matt1:17) · [2CO 12:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:2) · [GAL 2:1](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:1)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 1:17; 2 Corinthians 12:2; Galatians 2:1


## δέκατος (id: 001197000000000)

δέκατος
=======

δέκατος (G1182) — δεκάτη, δέκατον

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-η, \-ον

60\.57 · Number · First, Second, Third, Etc. \[Ordinals]

tenth tenth in a series involving either time, space, or set

[JHN 1:39](https://ref.ly/Luke1:39) · [REV 21:20](https://ref.ly/Jude21:20)

60\.65 · (δέκατον) · Number · Half, Third, Fourth \[Fractional Part]

tenth, tenth part a tenth part of an object, series, or mass In rendering ‘the tenth of the city fell’ in [REV 11:13](https://ref.ly/Jude11:13), it may be necessary in some languages to say ‘for every ten buildings, one building fell’ or ‘every tenth building in the city collapsed.’

[REV 11:13](https://ref.ly/Jude11:13)

60\.66 · (δεκάτη) · Number · Half, Third, Fourth \[Fractional Part]

## δεκατόω (id: 001198000000000)

δεκατόω
=======

δεκατόω (G1183) — δεκατόομαι

57\.115 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

to collect tithes, to exact tithes from to cause someone to pay a tenth In a number of languages there are problems involved in speaking of ‘a tenth,’ and accordingly there are difficulties in formulating expressions about ‘tithing.’ In some languages one may speak of ‘a tenth’ as ‘one part of ten parts’ or ‘one part together with nine parts.’ ‘To tithe’ may be rendered as ‘from ten parts to pay one part’ or ‘to pay one part and to keep nine parts.’

[HEB 7:6](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:6)

57\.114 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

to give a tenth, to tithe to give a tenth of one’s income In [HEB 7:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:9) it may be important to indicate clearly that it was not Levi himself who received the tenth but his descendants. Therefore, one may render the latter part of [HEB 7:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:9) as ‘Levi, whose descendants collect the tenth, also paid it.’

[HEB 7:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:9)

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 7:6; Hebrews 7:9


## δεκτός (id: 001199000000000)

δεκτός
======

δεκτός (G1184)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ή, \-όν 

|  |
| --- |

 δέχομαι

25\.85 · Attitudes and Emotions · Acceptable To, To Be Pleased With

pleasing, acceptable pertaining to that which is pleasing in view of its being acceptable In a number of languages it is necessary to restructure expressions containing ‘acceptable to’ or ‘pleasing to.’ For example, in [ACT 10:35](https://ref.ly/John10:35) it may be necessary to translate ‘God accepts whoever worships him and does what is right’ or ‘God is pleased with whoever worships him and does what is right.’ Similarly, in [1TI 2:3](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:3) one may translate ‘this is good, and God our Savior likes it’ or ‘... is happy because of it.’

[ACT 10:35](https://ref.ly/John10:35) · [PHP 4:18](https://ref.ly/Eph4:18)

34\.54 · Association · Welcome, Receive

one who is welcomed, one who is acceptable pertaining to being welcomed or acceptable In rendering this expression in [LUK 4:24](https://ref.ly/Mark4:24) it may be necessary to restructure the relationships somewhat radically, for example, ‘because people of a town do not wish to accept one of their fellow townsmen as a prophet.’

[LUK 4:19](https://ref.ly/Mark4:19) · [LUK 4:24](https://ref.ly/Mark4:24)

66\.9 · Proper, Improper

appropriate, proper pertaining to being appropriate or fitting, with the implication of being favorable

[2CO 6:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 10:35; Philippians 4:18; Luke 4:19; Luke 4:24; 2 Corinthians 6:2

[MAT 5:29](https://ref.ly/Matt5:29) · [MAT 5:30](https://ref.ly/Matt5:30) · [MAT 5:39](https://ref.ly/Matt5:39) · [MAT 20:21](https://ref.ly/Matt20:21) · [MAT 20:23](https://ref.ly/Matt20:23) · [MAT 22:44](https://ref.ly/Matt22:44) · [MAT 25:33](https://ref.ly/Matt25:33) · [MAT 25:34](https://ref.ly/Matt25:34) · [MAT 26:64](https://ref.ly/Matt26:64) · [MAT 27:29](https://ref.ly/Matt27:29) · [MAT 27:38](https://ref.ly/Matt27:38) · [MRK 10:37](https://ref.ly/Matt10:37) · [MRK 10:40](https://ref.ly/Matt10:40) · [MRK 12:36](https://ref.ly/Matt12:36) · [MRK 14:62](https://ref.ly/Matt14:62) · [MRK 15:27](https://ref.ly/Matt15:27) · [MRK 16:5](https://ref.ly/Matt16:5) · [MRK 16:19](https://ref.ly/Matt16:19) · [LUK 1:11](https://ref.ly/Mark1:11) · [LUK 6:6](https://ref.ly/Mark6:6) · [LUK 20:42](https://ref.ly/Mark20:42) · [LUK 22:50](https://ref.ly/Mark22:50) · [LUK 22:69](https://ref.ly/Mark22:69) · [LUK 23:33](https://ref.ly/Mark23:33) · [JHN 18:10](https://ref.ly/Luke18:10) · [JHN 21:6](https://ref.ly/Luke21:6) · [ACT 2:25](https://ref.ly/John2:25) · [ACT 2:34](https://ref.ly/John2:34) · [ACT 3:7](https://ref.ly/John3:7) · [ACT 5:31](https://ref.ly/John5:31) · [ACT 7:55](https://ref.ly/John7:55) · [ACT 7:56](https://ref.ly/John7:56) · [ROM 8:34](https://ref.ly/Acts8:34) · [EPH 1:20](https://ref.ly/Gal1:20) · [COL 3:1](https://ref.ly/Phil3:1) · [HEB 1:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:3) · [HEB 1:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:13) · [HEB 8:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:1) · [HEB 10:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:12) · [HEB 12:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:2) · [1PE 3:22](https://ref.ly/Jas3:22) · [REV 1:16](https://ref.ly/Jude1:16) · [REV 10:2](https://ref.ly/Jude10:2) · [REV 10:5](https://ref.ly/Jude10:5) · [REV 13:16](https://ref.ly/Jude13:16)

8\.32 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

**Collocation:** δεξιά

right hand an abbreviated reference to a person’s right hand, which is generally the dominant hand; positive associations as opposed to the left The expression in [MAT 6:3](https://ref.ly/Matt6:3) is idiomatic and means not letting others know about the good which one does (see [28\.74](#28.74)). The right hand is often spoken of idiomatically as ‘the good hand’ or ‘the strong hand.’ Sometimes it is called ‘the mouth hand,’ that is to say, the hand which one uses in eating.  
For δεξιά in the idiom δεξιὰς δίδωμι ‘to give the right hand’ ([GAL 2:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:9)), see [34\.42](#34.42).

[MAT 6:3](https://ref.ly/Matt6:3) · [MAT 27:29](https://ref.ly/Matt27:29) · [2CO 6:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:7) · [GAL 2:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:9) · [REV 1:17](https://ref.ly/Jude1:17) · [REV 1:20](https://ref.ly/Jude1:20) · [REV 2:1](https://ref.ly/Jude2:1) · [REV 5:1](https://ref.ly/Jude5:1) · [REV 5:7](https://ref.ly/Jude5:7)

76\.4 · Power, Force

**Collocation:** δεξιά

power (a figurative extension of meaning of δεξιός\[b] ‘right hand,’ [8\.32](#8.32)) power, with the added implication of authority

[ACT 2:33](https://ref.ly/John2:33)

34\.42 · Association · Establish or Confirm a Relation

**Collocation:** δεξιὰς δίδωμι

to make a covenant, to make an agreement (an idiom, literally: to give right hands) to acknowledge an agreement establishing some relation, normally involving the actual practice of shaking hands

[GAL 2:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:9)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:29; Matthew 5:30; Matthew 5:39; Matthew 20:21; Matthew 20:23; Matthew 22:44; Matthew 25:33; Matthew 25:34; Matthew 26:64; Matthew 27:29; Matthew 27:38; Mark 10:37; Mark 10:40; Mark 12:36; Mark 14:62; Mark 15:27; Mark 16:5; Mark 16:19; Luke 1:11; Luke 6:6; Luke 20:42; Luke 22:50; Luke 22:69; Luke 23:33; John 18:10; John 21:6; Acts 2:25; Acts 2:34; Acts 3:7; Acts 5:31; Acts 7:55; Acts 7:56; Romans 8:34; Ephesians 1:20; Colossians 3:1; Hebrews 1:3; Hebrews 1:13; Hebrews 8:1; Hebrews 10:12; Hebrews 12:2; 1 Peter 3:22; Revelation 1:16; Revelation 10:2; Revelation 10:5; Revelation 13:16; Matthew 6:3; 2 Corinthians 6:7; Galatians 2:9; Revelation 1:17; Revelation 1:20; Revelation 2:1; Revelation 5:1; Revelation 5:7; Acts 2:33


## δέομαι (id: 001204000000000)

δέομαι
======

δέομαι (G1189)

impf.3sg. ἐδεῖτο · aor. ἐδεήθην · impv. δεήθητι 

|  |
| --- |

 δέησις · ἐνδεής · προσδέομαι

33\.170 · Communication · Ask For, Request

to plead, to beg to ask for with urgency, with the implication of presumed need

6\.184 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

skin, hide skin of an animal, normally including attached hair and sometimes tanned In a number of languages it is important to distinguish clearly between tanned and untanned skins or hides. ## δεσμός (id: 001214000000000)

δεσμός
======

δεσμός (G1199)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-οῦ 

|  |
| --- |

 δέω

6\.14 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Binding and Fastening

bonds, chains, fetters any instrument or means of binding or tying; used for binding objects together or restraining prisoners In translating [ACT 16:26](https://ref.ly/John16:26) one may often use a descriptive phrase, for example, ‘those things that bound them’ or ‘things with which they were tied.’ It is generally more satisfactory, however, to employ wherever possible a more specific referent, for example, ‘ropes,’ ‘chains’ or ‘fetters.’

[LUK 8:29](https://ref.ly/Mark8:29) · [ACT 16:26](https://ref.ly/John16:26) · [ACT 26:29](https://ref.ly/John26:29) · [COL 4:18](https://ref.ly/Phil4:18) · [2TI 2:9](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:9) · [HEB 11:36](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:36) · [JUD 1:6](https://ref.ly/3John1:6)

37\.115 · Control, Rule · Imprison

to be in prison, imprisonment (figurative extension of meaning of δεσμός\[a] ‘bonds,’ [6\.14](#6.14)) the state of being in prison The state of being a prisoner is often expressed somewhat idiomatically, for example, ‘to be tied hand and foot,’ ‘to be chained like a dog,’ or ‘to look through iron bars.’

[ACT 20:23](https://ref.ly/John20:23) · [ACT 23:29](https://ref.ly/John23:29) · [ACT 26:31](https://ref.ly/John26:31) · [PHP 1:7](https://ref.ly/Eph1:7) · [PHP 1:13](https://ref.ly/Eph1:13) · [PHP 1:14](https://ref.ly/Eph1:14) · [PHP 1:17](https://ref.ly/Eph1:17) · [2TI 2:9](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:9) · [PHM 1:10](https://ref.ly/Titus1:10) · [PHM 1:13](https://ref.ly/Titus1:13) · [HEB 11:36](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:36)

23\.156 · Physiological Processes and States · Sickness, Disease, Weakness

illness (a figurative extension of meaning of δεσμός\[a] ‘bond,’ [6\.14](#6.14)) a state of physical incapacity or illness, usually as the result of some controlling supernatural force (in [LUK 13:16](https://ref.ly/Mark13:16), the result of the activity of Satan)

here, hither, come here extension toward a goal at or near the speaker and implying movement1

[MAT 19:21](https://ref.ly/Matt19:21) · [MRK 10:21](https://ref.ly/Matt10:21) · [LUK 18:22](https://ref.ly/Mark18:22) · [JHN 11:43](https://ref.ly/Luke11:43) · [ACT 7:3](https://ref.ly/John7:3) · [ACT 7:34](https://ref.ly/John7:34) · [REV 17:1](https://ref.ly/Jude17:1) · [REV 21:9](https://ref.ly/Jude21:9)

67\.43 · Time · A Point of Time with Reference to Other Points of Time: Before, Long Ago, Now, At the Same Time, When, About, After

 \-α, \-ον

| --- |

67\.180 · Time · Definite Units of Time: Year, Month, Week, Day, Hour

on the second day pertaining to the second of two days Some persons have interpreted δευτεραῖος as a period of two days, so that one may translate ‘after two days we came to Puteoli.’ Though general Greek usage does not seem to substantiate this meaning for δευτεραῖος, the context of [ACT 28:13](https://ref.ly/John28:13) may involve a span of two days.

[MAT 10:14](https://ref.ly/Matt10:14) · [MAT 10:40](https://ref.ly/Matt10:40) · [MAT 10:40](https://ref.ly/Matt10:40) · [MAT 10:40](https://ref.ly/Matt10:40) · [MAT 10:40](https://ref.ly/Matt10:40) · [MAT 10:41](https://ref.ly/Matt10:41) · [MAT 10:41](https://ref.ly/Matt10:41) · [MAT 18:5](https://ref.ly/Matt18:5) · [MAT 18:5](https://ref.ly/Matt18:5) · [MRK 6:11](https://ref.ly/Matt6:11) · [MRK 9:37](https://ref.ly/Matt9:37) · [MRK 9:37](https://ref.ly/Matt9:37) · [MRK 9:37](https://ref.ly/Matt9:37) · [MRK 9:37](https://ref.ly/Matt9:37) · [LUK 2:28](https://ref.ly/Mark2:28) · [LUK 9:5](https://ref.ly/Mark9:5) · [LUK 9:48](https://ref.ly/Mark9:48) · [LUK 9:48](https://ref.ly/Mark9:48) · [LUK 9:48](https://ref.ly/Mark9:48) · [LUK 9:48](https://ref.ly/Mark9:48) · [LUK 9:53](https://ref.ly/Mark9:53) · [LUK 10:8](https://ref.ly/Mark10:8) · [LUK 10:10](https://ref.ly/Mark10:10) · [LUK 16:4](https://ref.ly/Mark16:4) · [LUK 16:9](https://ref.ly/Mark16:9) · [JHN 4:45](https://ref.ly/Luke4:45) · [2CO 7:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:15) · [2CO 11:16](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:16) · [GAL 4:14](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:14) · [COL 4:10](https://ref.ly/Phil4:10) · [HEB 11:31](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:31) · [JAS 1:21](https://ref.ly/Heb1:21)

31\.51 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Accept As True

to receive readily, to accept, to believe to readily receive information and to regard it as true

[MAT 11:14](https://ref.ly/Matt11:14) · [MRK 10:15](https://ref.ly/Matt10:15) · [LUK 8:13](https://ref.ly/Mark8:13) · [LUK 18:17](https://ref.ly/Mark18:17) · [ACT 8:14](https://ref.ly/John8:14) · [ACT 11:1](https://ref.ly/John11:1) · [ACT 17:11](https://ref.ly/John17:11) · [1CO 2:14](https://ref.ly/Rom2:14) · [2CO 11:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:4) · [1TH 1:6](https://ref.ly/Col1:6) · [1TH 2:13](https://ref.ly/Col2:13) · [2TH 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:10)

18\.1 · Attachment · Grasp, Hold

to take hold of, to grasp, to grab to take hold of something or someone, with or without force A number of languages differ radically in terms for ‘taking hold of,’ depending upon whether force is employed, whether the object is a thing or an animate being, and whether the language incorporates into a verb of ‘taking hold of’ a classification as to the objects involved, for example, long and thin, round and flat, ball\-like, angular, or lumpy.

[LUK 16:6](https://ref.ly/Mark16:6) · [LUK 16:7](https://ref.ly/Mark16:7) · [LUK 22:17](https://ref.ly/Mark22:17)3 · [EPH 6:17](https://ref.ly/Gal6:17)

1 There may be some subtle distinction in meaning between δέχομαι\[a] on the one hand and λαμβάνω\[c] and λῆμψις on the other, in that the latter set of meanings may imply more active participation on the part of the one who receives or takes the gift, but this cannot be determined from existing contexts. 2 There are no doubt certain contextual constraints involved in the choice of ἀναδέχομαι\[a], ἀποδέχομαι\[a], ἐπιδέχομαι\[a], εἰσδέχομαι, ὑποδέχομαι, προσδέχομαι\[b], and παραδέχομαι\[b] in the sense that the spacial relationships involved in the welcoming of a guest can be reflected in the prepositional prefixes. For example, in [LUK 8:40](https://ref.ly/Mark8:40) the use of ἀποδέχομαι may focus upon the particular source, while ἐπιδέχομαι in [3JN 1:10](https://ref.ly/2John1:10) may be relevant in view of the fact that the believers are coming to a particular point. προσδέχομαι in [LUK 15:2](https://ref.ly/Mark15:2) may suggest a kind of reciprocal relationship which is established with outcasts, and παραδέχομαι in [ACT 15:4](https://ref.ly/John15:4) may simply point to spacial proximity. However, it would be wrong to insist upon clear distinctions in meaning based on the very limited number of contexts involved. Some of these same distinctions in spacial relations may exist for the set προσλαμβάνω\[e], παραλαμβάνω\[d], ἀπολαμβάνω\[d]. 3 LUK 22:17 It is possible that δέχομαι in [LUK 22:17](https://ref.ly/Mark22:17) may mean ‘to receive’ (see [57\.125](#57.125)).

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 3:21; Acts 7:38; Acts 7:59; Acts 22:5; Acts 28:21; 1 Corinthians 2:14; 2 Corinthians 6:1; 2 Corinthians 8:17; Philippians 4:18; 1 Thessalonians 1:6; 1 Thessalonians 2:13; James 1:21; Matthew 10:14; Matthew 10:40; Matthew 10:41; Matthew 18:5; Mark 6:11; Mark 9:37; Luke 2:28; Luke 9:5; Luke 9:48; Luke 9:53; Luke 10:8; Luke 10:10; Luke 16:4; Luke 16:9; John 4:45; 2 Corinthians 7:15; 2 Corinthians 11:16; Galatians 4:14; Colossians 4:10; Hebrews 11:31; Matthew 11:14; Mark 10:15; Luke 8:13; Luke 18:17; Acts 8:14; Acts 11:1; Acts 17:11; 2 Corinthians 11:4; 2 Thessalonians 2:10; Luke 16:6; Luke 16:7; Luke 22:17; Ephesians 6:17

37\.33 · Control, Rule · Compel, Force

to compel, to force to compel someone to act in a particular manner In some instances ἀναγκάζω and δέω\[c] may be rendered as ‘to cause it to be necessary for.’ In other instances a simple causative seems to be the closest equivalent. ## δῆμος (id: 001233000000000)

δῆμος

noun

 ἀποδημέω · ἀπόδημος · δημηγορέω · δημιουργός · δημόσιος · ἐκδημέω · ἐπιδημέω · παρεπίδημος · συνέκδημος

11\.78 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

assembly, gathering a group of citizens assembled for socio\-political activities It is possible that in ἐκκλησία\[c] there is somewhat more focus upon the people being together as a legal assembly, while in the case of δῆμος the emphasis is merely upon a meeting of citizens. ## δημόσιος (id: 001234000000000)

δημόσιος
========

δημόσιος (G1219)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-α, \-ον 

|  |
| --- |

 δῆμος

28\.66 · Know · Able To Be Known

public, open pertaining to being able to be known by the public The rendering of διακατηλέγχετο in [ACT 18:28](https://ref.ly/John18:28) provides the verbal correspondences ‘he ... refuted ... in ... debate.’ The term δημοσίᾳ indicates that the debates took place in public so that everyone could know or did know what was said and proven. It is, of course, possible to understand δημοσίᾳ only in the sense of ‘public setting,’ but in [ACT 18:28](https://ref.ly/John18:28) something more than mere setting seems to be implied.

[ACT 5:18](https://ref.ly/John5:18) · [ACT 16:37](https://ref.ly/John16:37) · [ACT 18:28](https://ref.ly/John18:28) · [ACT 20:20](https://ref.ly/John20:20)

## δηνάριον (id: 001235000000000)

δηνάριον
========

δηνάριον (G1220)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου

6\.75 · Artifacts · Money and Monetary Units

denarius a Roman silver coin equivalent to a days wage of a common laborer The practice of translating terms for coins with specific monetary values has differed widely in different languages at different times and in different contexts. One of the most serious problems has been the recent rapid inflation which has taken place in many parts of the world and which has thus made traditional renderings relatively meaningless or even absurd. For a number of years the silver content in an ancient denarius was equivalent to twenty cents U.S., but the value of silver has changed appreciably within recent times, and therefore any calculation based upon the value of silver content in ancient coins is misleading. Furthermore, in ancient times silver coins had proportionately far more buying power than the equivalent amount of silver would have today. Therefore, a number of translators have attempted in some measure to relate coinage to buying power, or perhaps better, to earning power. For example, in [MRK 6:37](https://ref.ly/Matt6:37) the reference to ‘two hundred denarii’ is sometimes translated as ‘the equivalent of 200 days’ wages’ or even ‘eight months of a laborer’s wages.’  
In [MAT 18:28](https://ref.ly/Matt18:28) the reference to ‘a hundred denarii’ is designed primarily to indicate the contrast between the enormous sum owed by one servant in contrast with the very small amount owed by the fellow servant. In this instance the contrast may be expressed in terms of ‘thousands of denarii’ in contrast with a ‘few denarii.’ In such a case the equivalent coinage may be turned into a local currency, for example, ‘thousands of dollars’ in contrast with a ‘few dollars.’ In a number of cases translators have attempted to avoid any specific reference to a particular coin and have simply spoken of ‘silver coins’ or ‘gold coins’ without indicating particular values. Under such circumstances a marginal note is sometimes employed in order to indicate the relative value of the currency.

[MAT 18:28](https://ref.ly/Matt18:28) · [MAT 20:2](https://ref.ly/Matt20:2) · [MAT 20:9](https://ref.ly/Matt20:9) · [MAT 20:10](https://ref.ly/Matt20:10) · [MAT 20:13](https://ref.ly/Matt20:13) · [MAT 22:19](https://ref.ly/Matt22:19) · [MRK 6:37](https://ref.ly/Matt6:37) · [MRK 12:15](https://ref.ly/Matt12:15) · [MRK 14:5](https://ref.ly/Matt14:5) · [LUK 7:41](https://ref.ly/Mark7:41) · [LUK 10:35](https://ref.ly/Mark10:35) · [LUK 20:24](https://ref.ly/Mark20:24) · [JHN 6:7](https://ref.ly/Luke6:7) · [JHN 12:5](https://ref.ly/Luke12:5) · [REV 6:6](https://ref.ly/Jude6:6) · [REV 6:6](https://ref.ly/Jude6:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 18:28; Matthew 20:2; Matthew 20:9; Matthew 20:10; Matthew 20:13; Matthew 22:19; Mark 6:37; Mark 12:15; Mark 14:5; Luke 7:41; Luke 10:35; Luke 20:24; John 6:7; John 12:5; Revelation 6:6

90\.38 · Case · Benefaction

90\.44 · Case · Reason Participant

because of, on account of, for this reason (with the accusative) a marker of a participant constituting the cause or reason for an event or state In [MRK 6:17](https://ref.ly/Matt6:17) Herodias clearly constituted the reason or cause for Herod putting John in prison, but there is a sense in which διὰ Ηρῳδιάδα may also indicate Herods purpose in trying to please Herodias, and therefore one may translate ‘for the sake of Herodias’ (see διά\[d], [90\.38](#90.38)).

67\.106 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

**Collocation:** διὰ βραχέων

a little while, for a little while, a short time, brief, briefly pertaining to a relatively brief extent of time4 In [HEB 13:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:22) the phrase διὰ βραχέων may refer to the act of sending the communication or the amount of time required to receive the communication, that is to say, to read the communication or to hear it read. 67\.15 · Time · A Point of Time without Reference to Other Points of Time: Time, Occasion, Ever, Often

**Collocation:** διὰ παντός

regularly, periodically (an idiom, literally: through all) a number of related points of time, occurring at regular intervals

[ACT 10:2](https://ref.ly/John10:2) · [HEB 9:6](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:6)

67\.86 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

**Collocation:** διὰ παντός

always, constantly, continually (an idiom, literally, through all) duration of time, either continuous or episodic, but without limits In some languages there may be problems involved in rendering ἀεί or διὰ παντός\[b], since there may be a basic distinction between (a) continuous activity and (b) activity which may be defined as episodic in that it regularly recurs in related episodes. For example, in [2CO 6:10](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:10) the fact of being glad may be related specifically to the occasions of being saddened, while in [MAT 18:10](https://ref.ly/Matt18:10) the focus of meaning is probably upon the continuous nature of the relation.

[MAT 18:10](https://ref.ly/Matt18:10) · [MRK 5:5](https://ref.ly/Matt5:5) · [LUK 24:53](https://ref.ly/Mark24:53) · [ACT 2:25](https://ref.ly/John2:25) · [ACT 24:16](https://ref.ly/John24:16) · [ROM 11:10](https://ref.ly/Acts11:10) · [HEB 13:15](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:15)

1 There are probably certain subtle distinctions between the use of διά\[c] in contrast with εἰς\[h] or ἐν\[p] as markers of means, but this cannot be clearly determined from existing contexts. 2 MAT 8:28 It is possible to interpret διά in [MAT 8:28](https://ref.ly/Matt8:28) as being a blend of two meanings, namely, extension along a path and passage through an area (see [84\.29](#84.29)). 3 The series of expressions indicating relative shortness of time may very well differ slightly, at least in connotative meaning, but on the basis of existing NT contexts it is not possible to determine significant denotative differences. The phrases in this series may be technically regarded as idioms, but functionally they are better classed as frozen phrases, which act essentially like morphological units.

## διάβολος (id: 001243000000000)

διάβολος
========

διάβολος (G1228)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ον 

|  |
| --- |

 βάλλω

12\.34 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

Devil, Satan (a title for the Devil, literally ‘slanderer’) the principal supernatural evil being1 In a number of languages there is a well known proper name for the Devil as the chief of all demons. In other instances, however, he is given a descriptive name, for example, ‘the ruler of the evil spirits,’ ‘the chief of the demons,’ ‘the truly bad one,’ ‘the left\-handed one’ (as the one who is opposed to all which is right or correct), ‘the no\-good one,’ ‘the avaricious one.’ In some instances a term for the Devil may be highly idiomatic as, for example, ‘the barking one,’ a reference to the Devil’s presumed activity in animal guise.  
Some translators have attempted to construct a term for Devil on the basis of the meaning of the Greek term διάβολος as ‘slanderer.’ This, however, has rarely been advisable, largely because in practically all languages there is a far more relevant way of speaking about the Devil. Other translators have attempted to render the term Devil by simply borrowing the form of the word from a dominant language, but this may also introduce complications, since one cannot always control the manner in which such a term will be understood. In one language, for example, the borrowed term ‘devil’ was identified simply as a small spirit that spreads fever among people, while in another area the borrowed term ended up meaning only a spirit which induces insanity. In this latter instance, the translators finally used an expression for the Devil which meant literally ‘the lord of all sin.’  
Some translators have employed for ‘Devil’ the proper name Satan, but this is often not a satisfactory solution. In one language in West Africa, for example, the term Satan had already been borrowed but was understood in the sense of the culture hero of the people and not as a designation for the chief of demons.

[MAT 4:1](https://ref.ly/Matt4:1) · [MAT 4:5](https://ref.ly/Matt4:5) · [MAT 4:8](https://ref.ly/Matt4:8) · [MAT 4:11](https://ref.ly/Matt4:11) · [MAT 13:39](https://ref.ly/Matt13:39) · [MAT 25:41](https://ref.ly/Matt25:41) · [LUK 4:2](https://ref.ly/Mark4:2) · [LUK 4:3](https://ref.ly/Mark4:3) · [LUK 4:6](https://ref.ly/Mark4:6) · [LUK 4:13](https://ref.ly/Mark4:13) · [LUK 8:12](https://ref.ly/Mark8:12) · [JHN 8:44](https://ref.ly/Luke8:44) · [JHN 13:2](https://ref.ly/Luke13:2) · [ACT 10:38](https://ref.ly/John10:38) · [ACT 13:10](https://ref.ly/John13:10) · [EPH 4:27](https://ref.ly/Gal4:27) · [EPH 6:11](https://ref.ly/Gal6:11) · [1TI 3:6](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:6) · [1TI 3:7](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:7) · [2TI 2:26](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:26) · [HEB 2:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:14) · [JAS 4:7](https://ref.ly/Heb4:7) · [1PE 5:8](https://ref.ly/Jas5:8) · [1JN 3:8](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:8) · [1JN 3:8](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:8) · [1JN 3:8](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:8) · [1JN 3:10](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:10) · [JUD 1:9](https://ref.ly/3John1:9) · [REV 2:10](https://ref.ly/Jude2:10) · [REV 12:9](https://ref.ly/Jude12:9) · [REV 12:12](https://ref.ly/Jude12:12) · [REV 20:2](https://ref.ly/Jude20:2) · [REV 20:10](https://ref.ly/Jude20:10)

12\.37 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

demon, evil spirit an evil supernatural being or spirit While in a number of languages the Devil may be spoken of as ‘the chief of the demons,’ sometimes the demons are simply called ‘the spirits of the Devil’ or ‘the servants of the Devil.’  
In a number of languages the difficulty in terminology for demons is not the absence of a term, but the abundance of different terms for different kinds of demons, each one of which may be responsible for particular kinds of human behavior, for example, insanity, depression, epilepsy, sex perversion, and violent assault. Sometimes demons are classified as ‘those of the home’ and ‘those of the forest,’ in which case the latter are normally regarded as more violent and virulent. When there is an abundance of different terms for demons and no generic term for all types of demons, one can usually select a class of demons which parallels most closely the descriptions of demon activity in the NT and use such a term with appropriate contextual qualifications so as to suggest that such a term is to be understood in a general sense.  
For another interpretation of διάβολος in [JHN 6:70](https://ref.ly/Luke6:70), see [88\.124](#88.124).

[JHN 6:70](https://ref.ly/Luke6:70)

33\.397 · Communication · Insult, Slander

slanderer (derivative of διαβάλλω ‘to slander,’ not occurring in the NT) one who engages in slander In [1TI 3:11](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:11) it may be appropriate to render διαβόλους as ‘gossipers.’

[1TI 3:11](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:11) · [2TI 3:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:3) · [TIT 2:3](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:3)

88\.124 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Bad, Evil, Harmful, Damaging

a devil (a figurative extension of meaning of διάβολος\[a] ‘Devil,’ [12\.34](#12.34)) a wicked person who has a number of characteristics typical of the Devil In some languages it would not be possible to translate [JHN 6:70](https://ref.ly/Luke6:70) literally as ‘one of you is a devil.’ The closest equivalent in such circumstances may be a simile, for example, ‘one of you is just like the Devil.’ For another interpretation of διάβολος in [JHN 6:70](https://ref.ly/Luke6:70), see [12\.37](#12.37).

[JHN 6:70](https://ref.ly/Luke6:70)

1 The terms διάβολος and Σατανᾶς appear to function both as titles and as proper names. This results from the fact that the referent in each instance is unique. In the text of the Greek NT Σατανᾶς was traditionally written with an initial capital letter, while διάβολος was normally written with a lower case initial letter, except for the occurrences of Διάβολος in [REV 12:9](https://ref.ly/Jude12:9) and [REV 20:2](https://ref.ly/Jude20:2).

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 4:1; Matthew 4:5; Matthew 4:8; Matthew 4:11; Matthew 13:39; Matthew 25:41; Luke 4:2; Luke 4:3; Luke 4:6; Luke 4:13; Luke 8:12; John 8:44; John 13:2; Acts 10:38; Acts 13:10; Ephesians 4:27; Ephesians 6:11; 1 Timothy 3:6; 1 Timothy 3:7; 2 Timothy 2:26; Hebrews 2:14; James 4:7; 1 Peter 5:8; 1 John 3:8; 1 John 3:10; Jude 1:9; Revelation 2:10; Revelation 12:9; Revelation 12:12; Revelation 20:2; Revelation 20:10; John 6:70; 1 Timothy 3:11; 2 Timothy 3:3; Titus 2:3

## διαθήκη (id: 001256000000000)

διαθήκη
=======

διαθήκη (G1242)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ης 

|  |
| --- |

 τίθημι

34\.43 · Association · Establish or Confirm a Relation

to make a covenant, to covenant together, making of a covenant to make a solemn agreement involving reciprocal benefits and responsibilities

[ROM 11:27](https://ref.ly/Acts11:27) · [HEB 8:6](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:6) · [HEB 8:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:8) · [HEB 8:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:9) · [HEB 8:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:9) · [HEB 8:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:10) · [HEB 10:16](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:16) · [HEB 12:24](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:24)

34\.44 · Association · Establish or Confirm a Relation

covenant, pact the verbal content of an agreement between two persons specifying reciprocal benefits and responsibilities In [LUK 1:72](https://ref.ly/Mark1:72), ποιῆσαι ἔλεος μετὰ τῶν πατέρων ἡμῶν καὶ μνησθῆναι διαθήκης ἁγίας αὐτοῦ ‘(God said he) would show mercy to our ancestors and remember his sacred covenant with them,’ it is possible that διαθήκη denotes either the making of the covenant ([34\.43](#34.43)) or the verbal formulation ([34\.44](#34.44)).  
In rendering the OT term brith, the Septuagint translators employed διαθήκη, literally ‘final will’ or ‘testament,’ in place of συνθήκη ‘contract,’ ‘agreement,’ since they evidently wished to emphasize the fact that the initiative for such a covenantal relationship existed with one person rather than being the result of negotiation and compromise.  
In many societies, and particularly in tribal ones, a covenant is a very significant bond between persons. It may, in fact, be the most important and lasting interpersonal relationship. It is seldom entered into lightly, for in many societies a covenant binds a person for a lifetime and may even involve willingness to die for the sake of the covenantal relationship.

[MAT 26:28](https://ref.ly/Matt26:28) · [MRK 14:24](https://ref.ly/Matt14:24) · [LUK 1:72](https://ref.ly/Mark1:72) · [LUK 22:20](https://ref.ly/Mark22:20) · [ACT 3:25](https://ref.ly/John3:25) · [ACT 7:8](https://ref.ly/John7:8) · [ROM 9:4](https://ref.ly/Acts9:4) · [1CO 11:25](https://ref.ly/Rom11:25) · [2CO 3:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:6) · [2CO 3:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:14) · [GAL 3:15](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:15) · [GAL 3:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:17) · [GAL 4:24](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:24) · [EPH 2:12](https://ref.ly/Gal2:12) · [HEB 7:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:22) · [HEB 9:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:4) · [HEB 9:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:4) · [HEB 9:15](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:15) · [HEB 9:15](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:15) · [HEB 10:16](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:16) · [HEB 10:29](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:29) · [HEB 12:24](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:24) · [HEB 13:20](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:20) · [REV 11:19](https://ref.ly/Jude11:19)

57\.124 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

will, testament (derivative of διατίθημι\[a] ‘to make a will,’ [57\.123](#57.123)) a legal document by which property is transferred by the deceased to an heir or heirs

[HEB 7:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:22) · [HEB 9:16](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:16) · [HEB 9:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:17) · [HEB 9:20](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 11:27; Hebrews 8:6; Hebrews 8:8; Hebrews 8:9; Hebrews 8:10; Hebrews 10:16; Hebrews 12:24; Matthew 26:28; Mark 14:24; Luke 1:72; Luke 22:20; Acts 3:25; Acts 7:8; Romans 9:4; 1 Corinthians 11:25; 2 Corinthians 3:6; 2 Corinthians 3:14; Galatians 3:15; Galatians 3:17; Galatians 4:24; Ephesians 2:12; Hebrews 7:22; Hebrews 9:4; Hebrews 9:15; Hebrews 10:29; Hebrews 13:20; Revelation 11:19; Hebrews 9:16; Hebrews 9:17; Hebrews 9:20

## διακονέω (id: 001262000000000)

διακονέω
========

διακονέω (G1247)

διακονία · διάκονος

35\.19 · Help, Care For · Serve

to serve, to render service, to help, service, help to render assistance or help by performing certain duties, often of a humble or menial nature In some languages it is essential in communicating the concept of ‘service’ to introduce a specific reference to ‘a servant,’ for example, ‘to help as a servant’ or ‘to assist as one who must,’ and in some contexts it may be useful to employ a phrase such as ‘to help in small things’ or ‘to do the low tasks.’  
In rendering [MAT 20:28](https://ref.ly/Matt20:28) it may be necessary to be somewhat more specific about those who serve or are served, for example, ‘the Son of Man did not come in order for people to serve him but in order to serve people.’

[MAT 20:28](https://ref.ly/Matt20:28) · [MAT 20:28](https://ref.ly/Matt20:28) · [MRK 10:45](https://ref.ly/Matt10:45) · [MRK 10:45](https://ref.ly/Matt10:45) · [LUK 10:40](https://ref.ly/Mark10:40) · [LUK 12:37](https://ref.ly/Mark12:37) · [LUK 17:8](https://ref.ly/Mark17:8) · [LUK 22:26](https://ref.ly/Mark22:26) · [LUK 22:27](https://ref.ly/Mark22:27) · [LUK 22:27](https://ref.ly/Mark22:27) · [JHN 12:26](https://ref.ly/Luke12:26) · [JHN 12:26](https://ref.ly/Luke12:26) · [ACT 19:22](https://ref.ly/John19:22) · [ROM 15:25](https://ref.ly/Acts15:25) · [2TI 1:18](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:18) · [PHM 1:13](https://ref.ly/Titus1:13) · [HEB 6:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:10) · [HEB 6:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:10) · [1PE 1:12](https://ref.ly/Jas1:12) · [1PE 4:10](https://ref.ly/Jas4:10) · [1PE 4:11](https://ref.ly/Jas4:11)

35\.37 · Help, Care For · Care For, Take Care Of

to take care of to take care of, by rendering humble service to In [MAT 25:44](https://ref.ly/Matt25:44), it may be possible to render ‘and we did not take care of you’ as ‘and we did not give you whatever you needed.’

[MAT 4:11](https://ref.ly/Matt4:11) · [MAT 25:44](https://ref.ly/Matt25:44) · [MAT 27:55](https://ref.ly/Matt27:55) · [MRK 1:13](https://ref.ly/Matt1:13) · [MRK 15:41](https://ref.ly/Matt15:41) · [LUK 8:3](https://ref.ly/Mark8:3) · [2CO 3:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:3) · [2CO 8:19](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:19) · [2CO 8:20](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:20) · [HEB 6:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:10) · [HEB 6:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:10)

to serve, to wait upon to serve food and drink to those who are eating

[MAT 8:15](https://ref.ly/Matt8:15) · [MAT 27:55](https://ref.ly/Matt27:55) · [MRK 1:31](https://ref.ly/Matt1:31) · [LUK 4:39](https://ref.ly/Mark4:39) · [JHN 12:2](https://ref.ly/Luke12:2)

53\.66 · Religious Activities · Roles and Functions

to be a deacon, to minister to to serve God in some special way, such as a deacon It seems quite evident that διακονέω\[d] involved a number of different functions as persons served others, especially in connection with relief to the poor. In some instances it may be best to translate διακονέω\[d] as ‘to have responsibility to help others’ or ‘to be responsible to take care of the needs of believers.’

57\.230 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Keep Records

**Collocation:** διακονέω τραπέζαις

to handle finances (an idiom, literally: to serve tables) to be responsible for financial aspects of an enterprise It is also possible to interpret the phrase διακονέω τραπέζαις not as an idiom but simply as ‘to wait on tables, to serve meals’ (see [23\.26](#23.26) and [46\.13](#46.13)), but even so the context relates to caring for needs.

[ACT 6:2](https://ref.ly/John6:2)

## διακονία (id: 001263000000000)

διακονία
========

διακονία (G1248)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ας 

|  |
| --- |

 διακονέω

35\.19 · Help, Care For · Serve

to serve, to render service, to help, service, help to render assistance or help by performing certain duties, often of a humble or menial nature In some languages it is essential in communicating the concept of ‘service’ to introduce a specific reference to ‘a servant,’ for example, ‘to help as a servant’ or ‘to assist as one who must,’ and in some contexts it may be useful to employ a phrase such as ‘to help in small things’ or ‘to do the low tasks.’  
In rendering ‘your service’ in [REV 2:19](https://ref.ly/Jude2:19), it may be necessary to say ‘how you help others’ or ‘how you serve others.’

[ROM 12:7](https://ref.ly/Acts12:7) · [ROM 15:31](https://ref.ly/Acts15:31) · [2CO 11:8](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:8) · [EPH 4:12](https://ref.ly/Gal4:12) · [2TI 4:11](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:11) · [HEB 1:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:14) · [REV 2:19](https://ref.ly/Jude2:19)

35\.21 · Help, Care For · Serve

ministry, task (derivative of διακονέω\[a] ‘to serve,’ [35\.19](#35.19)) the role or position of serving

[ACT 1:17](https://ref.ly/John1:17) · [ACT 1:25](https://ref.ly/John1:25) · [ACT 6:4](https://ref.ly/John6:4) · [ACT 20:24](https://ref.ly/John20:24) · [ACT 21:19](https://ref.ly/John21:19) · [ROM 11:13](https://ref.ly/Acts11:13) · [ROM 12:7](https://ref.ly/Acts12:7) · [ROM 12:7](https://ref.ly/Acts12:7) · [1CO 12:5](https://ref.ly/Rom12:5) · [1CO 16:15](https://ref.ly/Rom16:15) · [2CO 3:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:7) · [2CO 3:8](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:8) · [2CO 3:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:9) · [2CO 3:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:9) · [2CO 4:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:1) · [2CO 5:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:18) · [2CO 6:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:3) · [2CO 8:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:4) · [COL 4:17](https://ref.ly/Phil4:17) · [1TI 1:12](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:12) · [2TI 4:5](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:5) · [HEB 1:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:14)

35\.38 · Help, Care For · Care For, Take Care Of

provision for taking care of, arrangement for support a procedure for taking care of the needs of people For another interpretation of διακονία in [ACT 6:1](https://ref.ly/John6:1), see [57\.119](#57.119).

[ACT 6:1](https://ref.ly/John6:1) · [2CO 9:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:12)

46\.13 · Household Activities

to serve, to wait upon to serve food and drink to those who are eating

[LUK 10:40](https://ref.ly/Mark10:40)

57\.119 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

contribution, help, support (semantic derivative of διακονία\[a] ‘to serve,’ [35\.19](#35.19)) money given to help someone in need For another interpretation of διακονέω in [ACT 6:1](https://ref.ly/John6:1), see [35\.38](#35.38).

[ACT 6:1](https://ref.ly/John6:1) · [ACT 11:29](https://ref.ly/John11:29) · [ACT 12:25](https://ref.ly/John12:25) · [2CO 9:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:1) · [2CO 9:13](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:13)

## διάκονος (id: 001264000000000)

διάκονος
========

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 διακονέω

35\.20 · Help, Care For · Serve

servant (derivative of διακονέω\[a] ‘to serve,’ [35\.19](#35.19)) a person who renders service In rendering θεράπων, ὑπηρέτης, and διάκονος\[a] in the sense of ‘servant,’ it is important to avoid a term which would be too specific, for example, ‘one who serves meals’ or ‘one who works around the house.’ It may, in fact, be necessary to use an expression which means essentially ‘helper.’

## διακούω (id: 001266000000000)

διακούω
=======

διακούω (G1251)

ἀκούω

56\.13 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Judicial Hearing, Inquiry

to hear a case, to provide a legal hearing, to hear a case in court to give a judicial hearing in a legal matter1 In some languages the most satisfactory way of speaking about ‘a court hearing’ is to describe the relationship between the principal participants. This may sometimes be done by translating ‘for a judge to listen to an accuser and a defender.’

[ACT 23:35](https://ref.ly/John23:35)

1 ἀκούω\[g] and διακούω apparently differ somewhat in meaning from ἀνακρίνω\[b] ([56\.12](#56.12)) in that the former two seem to be more neutral in connotation and do not appear to imply later condemnation.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 23:35


## διακρίνω (id: 001267000000000)

διακρίνω
========

διακρίνω (G1252) — διακρίνομαι

aor.pass. διεκρίθην 

|  |
| --- |

 κρίνω

30\.109 · Think · To Distinguish, To Evaluate, To Judge

to judge carefully, to evaluate carefully to make a judgment on the basis of careful and detailed information1

[MAT 16:3](https://ref.ly/Matt16:3) · [1CO 6:5](https://ref.ly/Rom6:5) · [1CO 11:29](https://ref.ly/Rom11:29) · [1CO 11:31](https://ref.ly/Rom11:31) · [1CO 14:29](https://ref.ly/Rom14:29)

30\.99 · Think · To Choose, To Select, To Prefer

to prefer, to judge as superior, to regard as more valuable to judge something to be better than something else, and hence, to prefer Superiority is often expressed in terms of ‘being better,’ but in some languages it is designated by means of a phrase meaning ‘to surpass,’ so that the question in [1CO 4:7](https://ref.ly/Rom4:7) may be rendered as ‘who judges that you surpass others?’

[1CO 4:7](https://ref.ly/Rom4:7)

30\.113 · Think · To Distinguish, To Evaluate, To Judge

to make a distinction, to judge that there is a difference to judge that there is a difference or distinction In some languages it may be best to render this statement in [ACT 15:9](https://ref.ly/John15:9) as ‘he did not think that we and they are different.’

[ACT 11:12](https://ref.ly/John11:12) · [ACT 15:9](https://ref.ly/John15:9) · [1CO 4:7](https://ref.ly/Rom4:7) · [JAS 2:4](https://ref.ly/Heb2:4)

31\.37 · (διακρίνομαι\[a]) · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Believe To Be True

to doubt, to be uncertain about, doubt to think that something may not be true or certain In a number of languages ‘doubt’ is expressed by means of idioms, for example, ‘to have two thoughts’ or ‘to think only perhaps’ or ‘to believe only a little’ or ‘to question one’s heart about.’

[MAT 21:21](https://ref.ly/Matt21:21) · [MRK 11:23](https://ref.ly/Matt11:23) · [ACT 10:20](https://ref.ly/John10:20) · [ROM 4:20](https://ref.ly/Acts4:20) · [ROM 14:23](https://ref.ly/Acts14:23) · [JAS 1:6](https://ref.ly/Heb1:6) · [JAS 1:6](https://ref.ly/Heb1:6) · [JUD 1:22](https://ref.ly/3John1:22)

33\.444 · (διακρίνομαι\[b]) · Communication · Dispute, Debate

to dispute, to debate about, contention, dispute to dispute with someone on the basis of different judgments

[JUD 1:9](https://ref.ly/3John1:9)

33\.412 · (διακρίνομαι\[c]) · Communication · Criticize

to criticize to express disapproval of what someone has done It is possible to interpret the meaning of διακρίνομαι in [ACT 11:2](https://ref.ly/John11:2) as being merely adverse judgment, but since this judgment was clearly voiced, διακρίνομαι implies more than mere judgment. The direct expression of an adverse judgment may be best rendered in English as ‘to criticize.’

[ACT 11:2](https://ref.ly/John11:2)

1 The meanings of κρίνω\[c] ([30\.108](#30.108)), ἀνακρίνω\[d] and διακρίνω\[a] ([30\.109](#30.109)) are all closely related to the process of learning and of understanding, and in some contexts the meanings shade one into the other.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 16:3; 1 Corinthians 6:5; 1 Corinthians 11:29; 1 Corinthians 11:31; 1 Corinthians 14:29; 1 Corinthians 4:7; Acts 11:12; Acts 15:9; James 2:4; Matthew 21:21; Mark 11:23; Acts 10:20; Romans 4:20; Romans 14:23; James 1:6; Jude 1:22; Jude 1:9; Acts 11:2

to remain, to continue, to continue to exist, to still be in existence to continue to exist1

1 It is possible that διαμένω\[c] is somewhat more emphatic in meaning than μένω\[c].

## διανεύω (id: 001284000000000)

διανεύω
=======

διανεύω (G1269)

νεύω

33\.485 · Communication · Non\-Verbal Communication

to gesture, to motion, to nod, to beckon to signal to someone by means of part of the body, especially by means of the head or hands1 In a number of languages it is necessary to be quite specific with regard to types of gestures or motions of the head or hands and arms. For example, in [JHN 13:24](https://ref.ly/Luke13:24) there is an obvious question involved, and this may require in some languages a particular signal by means of the hands or face. The same would be true in the case of [LUK 1:62](https://ref.ly/Mark1:62). In [LUK 1:22](https://ref.ly/Mark1:22) the gesture would have to be something which would explain or indicate Zechariah’s inability to speak, while in [LUK 5:7](https://ref.ly/Mark5:7) quite another gesture would no doubt be called for, since the persons involved were at quite a distance from one another.

[LUK 1:22](https://ref.ly/Mark1:22)

1 There are no doubt certain subtle differences of meaning between νεύω, ἐννεύω, διανεύω, and κατανεύω, but such distinctions are not evident from existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:22

 νοέω

30\.15 · Think · To Think, Thought

For example, in [LUK 11:17](https://ref.ly/Mark11:17) one may translate as ‘but Jesus knew what they were thinking.’

## διάνοια (id: 001286000000000)

διάνοια
=======

διάνοια (G1271)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ας 

|  |
| --- |

 νοέω

26\.14 · Psychological Faculties

mind the psychological faculty of understanding, reasoning, thinking, and deciding In some languages there is no noun such as English mind, and therefore one must use a verb expression meaning ‘to think,’ ‘to reason,’ or ‘to understand,’ depending upon the particular context. In some languages the closest equivalent of ‘mind’ may be a figurative extension of a term meaning ‘head,’ but more often than not, thinking is regarded as being in some other part of the body, for example, ‘heart’ or ‘liver.’

[MAT 22:37](https://ref.ly/Matt22:37) · [MRK 12:30](https://ref.ly/Matt12:30) · [LUK 10:27](https://ref.ly/Mark10:27) · [EPH 2:3](https://ref.ly/Gal2:3) · [EPH 4:18](https://ref.ly/Gal4:18) · [HEB 8:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:10) · [HEB 10:16](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:16) · [1PE 1:13](https://ref.ly/Jas1:13)

30\.5 · Think · To Think, Thought

way of thinking, disposition, manner of thought, attitude a particular manner or way of thinking In a number of languages it may be necessary to render ‘way of thinking’ by a clause, for example, ‘how people think.’ In the case of [1PE 4:1](https://ref.ly/Jas4:1), it may be necessary to translate ‘you too must strengthen yourselves by thinking just like Christ thought.’

[COL 1:21](https://ref.ly/Phil1:21)

30\.15 · Think · To Think, Thought

thought, what is thought, opinion the content of thinking and reasoning In a number of languages it is simply not possible to find noun\-like words for thinking or reasoning and therefore it may be necessary to use a verb equivalent throughout. For example, in [LUK 11:17](https://ref.ly/Mark11:17) one may translate as ‘but Jesus knew what they were thinking.’

[LUK 1:51](https://ref.ly/Mark1:51) · [2PE 3:1](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:1) · [1JN 5:20](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 22:37; Mark 12:30; Luke 10:27; Ephesians 2:3; Ephesians 4:18; Hebrews 8:10; Hebrews 10:16; 1 Peter 1:13; Colossians 1:21; Luke 1:51; 2 Peter 3:1; 1 John 5:20

27\.49 · Learn · Be Willing To Learn

**Collocation:** διανοίγω τὴν καρδίαν · διανοίγω τὸν νοῦν

to open someone’s mind, to cause someone to be open\-minded (idioms, literally: to open the mind, and: to open the heart) to cause someone to be willing to learn and evaluate fairly It is rare that one can speak literally of ‘opening the mind’ or ‘opening the heart.’ It is sometimes possible to use an expression such as ‘to cause the mind to see’ or ‘to cause the heart to know’ or ‘... to recognize.’ In some languages, however, ‘to open the mind’ or ‘to open the heart’ may refer to murderous violence.

| --- |

 ῥήγνυμι

19\.32 · Physical Impact · Split, Tear

to tear, to rip to tear or rip in two (as of clothing)1 In the NT tearing of clothing was a symbol of horror associated with sacrilege. In many cultures, however, the tearing of clothing may be associated only with insanity. It may therefore be important to add a phrase in describing ‘the tearing of clothing’ in order to mark the significance, for example, ‘to show horror’ ([MAT 26:65](https://ref.ly/Matt26:65), [ACT 14:14](https://ref.ly/John14:14)) and in the OT ‘to show mourning’ ([GEN 37:34](https://ref.ly/Gen37:34), [JDG 11:35](https://ref.ly/Judg11:35)).

## διασπορά (id: 001305000000000)

διασπορά
========

διασπορά (G1290)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ᾶς 

|  |
| --- |

 σπείρω

15\.137 · Linear Movement · Disperse, Scatter

region in which people are scattered, diaspora (derivative of διασπείρω ‘to scatter,’ [15\.136](#15.136)) the region or area in which persons have been scattered (particularly a reference to the nation of Israel which had been scattered throughout the ancient world) For the most part, the phrase ταῖς δώδεκα φυλαῖς in [JAS 1:1](https://ref.ly/Heb1:1) has been interpreted as a reference to believers in Christ. In translating, one may render the term διασπορά as ‘in all the regions where they have been scattered,’ thus rendering this expression in [JAS 1:1](https://ref.ly/Heb1:1) as ‘greetings to all of God’s people in all of the regions in which they have been scattered.’

88\.264 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Licentiousness, Perversion

In rendering διαστρέφω as ‘to pervert,’ one should not understand the meaning in terms of ‘sexual perversion.’ In speaking of ‘perverting our people’ in [LUK 23:2](https://ref.ly/Mark23:2), it would be better in most languages to translate ‘to cause our people to go astray’ or ‘to cause them to do what they certainly should not do.’

[MAT 17:17](https://ref.ly/Matt17:17) · [LUK 9:41](https://ref.ly/Mark9:41) · [LUK 23:2](https://ref.ly/Mark23:2) · [ACT 13:10](https://ref.ly/John13:10) · [ACT 20:30](https://ref.ly/John20:30) · [PHP 2:15](https://ref.ly/Eph2:15)

13\.46 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · State

to turn away from, to divert from to cause a state to cease by a diversion to some other state, usually with the implication of a wrong state

[ACT 13:8](https://ref.ly/John13:8)

1 διαστρέφω\[a] apparently differs somewhat in meaning from ἀποστρέφω\[a] ([31\.70](#31.70)) in emphasizing the effectiveness or thoroughness of the manner in which someone changes the belief of someone else.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 23:2; Matthew 17:17; Luke 9:41; Acts 13:10; Acts 20:30; Philippians 2:15; Acts 13:8
