## διατροφή (id: 001319000000000)

διατροφή
========

διατροφή (G1305)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ῆς 

|  |
| --- |

 τρέφω

5\.1 · Foods and Condiments · Food

food any kind of food or nourishment1 Almost all languages have at least a few general terms for food, though these may be derived from verbal expressions meaning essentially ‘that which is eaten.’ In some instances a distinction may be made between ‘that which is chewed’ and ‘that which is drunk,’ and it may therefore be important in certain contexts to speak of food in general by a phrase meaning ‘that which is either chewed or drunk.’ If one fails to include both types of food, the reader might interpret a passage such as [MAT 6:11](https://ref.ly/Matt6:11) as requesting only solid foods.  
In the place of a general term or phrase such as ‘that which is eaten’ or ‘that which is consumed,’ some languages generalize the meaning of a particular term. For example, in certain parts of the Orient the term meaning specifically ‘rice’ also refers to ‘food’ in general. In fact, some persons will declare, ‘I have not eaten!’ if they have not had rice as part of a meal. A similar type of meaning has developed in English with respect to ‘bread.’ For example, in rendering [LUK 4:4](https://ref.ly/Mark4:4) (οὐκ ἐπ’ ἄρτῳ μόνῳ ζήσεται ὁ ἄνθρωπος ‘man shall not live by bread alone’) it would be wrong to employ a strictly literal rendering, since this might mean simply that people should not live on a diet consisting solely of bread. The meaning of [LUK 4:4](https://ref.ly/Mark4:4) is, of course, ‘to live means more than merely eating.’

[1TI 6:8](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:8)2

1 There are no doubt certain subtle differences of meaning in the various terms listed here as meaning ‘food,’ but it is impossible to determine such distinctions in meaning from NT contexts. Perhaps τροφή and διατροφή are somewhat more generic in meaning and may suggest a greater emphasis upon nourishment (see footnote b). At the same time, βρῶσις\[c] and βρῶμα\[a] may imply solid substantive food, but it is difficult, if not impossible, to argue for such subtle connotative distinctions in meanings which are essentially generic. 2 1TI 6:8 It is possible that τροφή and διατροφή focus primarily upon the meaning of food as nourishment, and in [1TI 6:8](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:8) and [MAT 10:10](https://ref.ly/Matt10:10) it would be perfectly appropriate to use a translation meaning ‘nourishment’ rather than merely ‘food.’

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Timothy 6:8

## διδακτός (id: 001333000000000)

διδακτός
========

διδακτός (G1318)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ή, \-όν 

|  |
| --- |

 διδάσκω

33\.227 · Communication · Teach

taught, instructed (derivative of διδάσκω ‘to teach,’ [33\.224](#33.224)) pertaining to that which is taught The expression ἐν διδακτοῖς ἀνθρωπίνης σοφίας λόγοις in [1CO 2:13](https://ref.ly/Rom2:13) is semantically complex. One may interpret this to mean ‘by means of words used in teaching human wisdom’ or ‘by means of words concerning human wisdom as it is taught.’ Though grammatically διδακτοῖς ‘taught’ goes with λόγοις ‘words,’ there is a very close semantic connection between διδακτοῖς and ἀνθρωπίνης σοφίας ‘human wisdom.’

[JHN 6:45](https://ref.ly/Luke6:45) · [1CO 2:13](https://ref.ly/Rom2:13) · [1CO 2:13](https://ref.ly/Rom2:13)

## διδασκαλία (id: 001334000000000)

διδασκαλία
==========

διδασκαλία (G1319)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ας 

|  |
| --- |

 διδάσκω

33\.224 · Communication · Teach

to teach, teaching to provide instruction in a formal or informal setting The equivalent of ‘to teach’ in many languages is simply a causative form of a verb meaning ‘to learn’ or ‘to know,’ for example, ‘to cause to learn’ or ‘to cause to know.’ In choosing a term for ‘to teach’ it is important to avoid an expression which will denote merely classroom activity.

[MRK 7:7](https://ref.ly/Matt7:7) · [ROM 12:7](https://ref.ly/Acts12:7) · [ROM 15:4](https://ref.ly/Acts15:4) · [1TI 4:13](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:13) · [1TI 4:16](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:16) · [1TI 5:17](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:17) · [1TI 6:3](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:3) · [2TI 3:10](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:10) · [2TI 3:16](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:16) · [2TI 4:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:3) · [TIT 1:9](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:9) · [TIT 2:7](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:7)

## διδάσκαλος (id: 001335000000000)

διδάσκαλος
==========

διδάσκαλος (G1320)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 διδάσκω

33\.243 · Communication · Teach

teacher, instructor (derivative of διδάσκω ‘to teach,’ [33\.224](#33.224)) one who provides instruction

## διδάσκω (id: 001336000000000)

διδάσκω
=======

διδάσκω (G1321)

aor.pass. ἐδιδάχθην 

|  |
| --- |

 διδακτικός · διδακτός · διδασκαλία · διδάσκαλος · διδαχή · ἑτεροδιδασκαλέω · θεοδίδακτος · καλοδιδάσκαλος · νομοδιδάσκαλος · ψευδοδιδάσκαλος

33\.224 · Communication · Teach

to teach, teaching to provide instruction in a formal or informal setting The equivalent of ‘to teach’ in many languages is simply a causative form of a verb meaning ‘to learn’ or ‘to know,’ for example, ‘to cause to learn’ or ‘to cause to know.’ In choosing a term for ‘to teach’ it is important to avoid an expression which will denote merely classroom activity.

## διδαχή (id: 001337000000000)

διδαχή
======

διδαχή (G1322)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ῆς 

|  |
| --- |

 διδάσκω

33\.224 · Communication · Teach

to teach, teaching to provide instruction in a formal or informal setting The equivalent of ‘to teach’ in many languages is simply a causative form of a verb meaning ‘to learn’ or ‘to know,’ for example, ‘to cause to learn’ or ‘to cause to know.’ In choosing a term for ‘to teach’ it is important to avoid an expression which will denote merely classroom activity.

[MAT 7:28](https://ref.ly/Matt7:28) · [MAT 22:33](https://ref.ly/Matt22:33) · [MRK 1:22](https://ref.ly/Matt1:22) · [MRK 4:2](https://ref.ly/Matt4:2) · [MRK 11:18](https://ref.ly/Matt11:18) · [MRK 12:38](https://ref.ly/Matt12:38) · [LUK 4:32](https://ref.ly/Mark4:32) · [1CO 14:6](https://ref.ly/Rom14:6) · [1CO 14:26](https://ref.ly/Rom14:26) · [2TI 4:2](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:2) · [TIT 1:9](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:9) · [HEB 13:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:9)

33\.236 · Communication · Teach

what is taught, doctrine, teaching (derivative of διδάσκω ‘to teach,’ [33\.224](#33.224)) the content of what is taught

[MAT 7:28](https://ref.ly/Matt7:28) · [MAT 16:12](https://ref.ly/Matt16:12) · [MAT 22:33](https://ref.ly/Matt22:33) · [MRK 1:22](https://ref.ly/Matt1:22) · [MRK 1:27](https://ref.ly/Matt1:27) · [MRK 11:18](https://ref.ly/Matt11:18) · [LUK 4:32](https://ref.ly/Mark4:32) · [JHN 7:16](https://ref.ly/Luke7:16) · [JHN 7:17](https://ref.ly/Luke7:17) · [JHN 18:19](https://ref.ly/Luke18:19) · [ACT 2:42](https://ref.ly/John2:42) · [ACT 5:28](https://ref.ly/John5:28) · [ACT 13:12](https://ref.ly/John13:12) · [ACT 17:19](https://ref.ly/John17:19) · [ROM 6:17](https://ref.ly/Acts6:17) · [ROM 16:17](https://ref.ly/Acts16:17) · [1CO 14:6](https://ref.ly/Rom14:6) · [1CO 14:26](https://ref.ly/Rom14:26) · [2TI 4:2](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:2) · [TIT 1:9](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:9) · [HEB 13:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:9) · [2JN 1:9](https://ref.ly/1John1:9) · [2JN 1:9](https://ref.ly/1John1:9) · [2JN 1:10](https://ref.ly/1John1:10) · [REV 2:14](https://ref.ly/Jude2:14) · [REV 2:15](https://ref.ly/Jude2:15) · [REV 2:24](https://ref.ly/Jude2:24)

## δίδραχμον (id: 001338000000000)

δίδραχμον
=========

δίδραχμον (G1323)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 δύο \+ δραχμή 

|  |
| --- |

 δράσσομαι

57\.181 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Tax, Tribute

two\-drachma piece, temple tax the tax required of every male Jew from the age of twenty onward; to support the temple The two\-drachma coin referred to in [MAT 17:24](https://ref.ly/Matt17:24) was approximately equivalent to two denarii. The meaning of δίδραχμον is treated here in Domain 57 rather than in Domain 6 (where the value of other coins is discussed) since the focus of the meaning of δίδραχμον is the required Temple tax rather than the value or form of the coin itself.

[MAT 17:24](https://ref.ly/Matt17:24) · [MAT 17:24](https://ref.ly/Matt17:24)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 17:24

1 In this meaning δίδωμι serves primarily as a so\-called empty verb. The event is to be found in the so\-called object of the verb. 2 δίδωμι seems to imply a benevolent purpose in the action of assigning someone to a role. 3 By setting up certain highly generic meanings for βλαστάνω, δίδωμι, ἀποδίδωμι, and ποιέω, it would be possible to treat the phrase compounds in this series as being semantically endocentric. However, it seems more satisfactory to regard them as what might be called low\-grade idioms with specialized meanings of the semantically head expressions.

## διεγείρω (id: 001341000000000)

διεγείρω
========

aor. διήγειρα · aor.pass.ptc. διεγερθείς 

|  |
| --- |

to cause to wake up, to awaken someone, to wake up someone to cause someone to awaken

[LUK 8:24](https://ref.ly/Mark8:24)

90\.52 · Case · Agent in a Causative Role Marked by Verbs

to cause a marker of a causative relation, with the implication of a significant change in state

[2PE 1:13](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:13) · [2PE 3:1](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:1)

23\.74 · (διεγείρομαι\[a]) · Physiological Processes and States · Sleep, Waking

to wake up, to become awake to become awake after sleeping

[MRK 4:39](https://ref.ly/Matt4:39) · [LUK 8:24](https://ref.ly/Mark8:24)

14\.20 · (διεγείρομαι\[b]) · Physical Events and States · Events Involving Liquids and Dry Masses

to become rough, to become stormy (a figurative extension of meaning of διεγείρομαι\[a] ‘to become awake from sleep,’ [23\.74](#23.74)) to become rough, in reference to a surface of water In describing a rough surface of a body of water, one may say in some languages ‘there were many waves’ or ‘the waves were very big.’ In other languages one may speak of a rough surface of a body of water by an idiomatic expression, for example, ‘the face of the water was foaming’ or ‘the water was angry.’

[JHN 6:18](https://ref.ly/Luke6:18)

## διενθυμέομαι (id: 001342000000000)

## διέρχομαι (id: 001346000000000)

διέρχομαι
=========

διέρχομαι (G1330)

fut. διελεύσομαι · aor. διῆλθον · inf. διελθεῖν · pf. διελήλυθα · ptc. διεληλυθώς 

|  |
| --- |

 ἔρχομαι

15\.17 · Linear Movement · Move, Come/Go

to move on to, to go on to to complete movement in a particular direction It would also be possible to translate διέρχομαι in [ACT 11:19](https://ref.ly/John11:19) as ‘arrived’ or ‘finally reached.’

[LUK 2:15](https://ref.ly/Mark2:15) · [JHN 4:15](https://ref.ly/Luke4:15) · [ACT 9:38](https://ref.ly/John9:38) · [ACT 11:19](https://ref.ly/John11:19) · [ACT 18:27](https://ref.ly/John18:27) · [ACT 19:1](https://ref.ly/John19:1) · [ROM 5:12](https://ref.ly/Acts5:12) · [2CO 1:16](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:16) · [HEB 4:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:14)

15\.21 · Linear Movement · Travel, Journey

to travel around through, to journey all through to travel around through an area, with the implication of both extensive and thorough movement throughout an area In order to express the meaning of διοδεύω, διαπορεύομαι\[a], and διέρχομαι\[b] in these types of contexts, it may be necessary in some languages to say ‘he went from one town to another’ or, as in [ACT 13:6](https://ref.ly/John13:6), ‘he travelled to all the places on the island’ or ‘... to the various towns on the island.’

[MAT 12:43](https://ref.ly/Matt12:43) · [LUK 4:30](https://ref.ly/Mark4:30) · [LUK 5:15](https://ref.ly/Mark5:15) · [LUK 9:6](https://ref.ly/Mark9:6) · [LUK 11:24](https://ref.ly/Mark11:24) · [LUK 17:11](https://ref.ly/Mark17:11) · [LUK 19:1](https://ref.ly/Mark19:1) · [LUK 19:4](https://ref.ly/Mark19:4) · [ACT 8:4](https://ref.ly/John8:4) · [ACT 8:40](https://ref.ly/John8:40) · [ACT 9:32](https://ref.ly/John9:32) · [ACT 10:38](https://ref.ly/John10:38) · [ACT 13:6](https://ref.ly/John13:6) · [ACT 13:14](https://ref.ly/John13:14) · [ACT 14:24](https://ref.ly/John14:24) · [ACT 15:3](https://ref.ly/John15:3) · [ACT 15:41](https://ref.ly/John15:41) · [ACT 16:6](https://ref.ly/John16:6) · [ACT 17:23](https://ref.ly/John17:23) · [ACT 18:23](https://ref.ly/John18:23) · [ACT 19:21](https://ref.ly/John19:21) · [ACT 20:2](https://ref.ly/John20:2) · [ACT 20:25](https://ref.ly/John20:25) · [1CO 16:5](https://ref.ly/Rom16:5) · [1CO 16:5](https://ref.ly/Rom16:5)

15\.31 · Linear Movement · Pass, Cross Over, Go Through, Go Around

to cross over, to go over to move from one side to another of some geographical object (for example, body of water, chasm, valley, etc.)

[MRK 4:35](https://ref.ly/Matt4:35) · [LUK 8:22](https://ref.ly/Mark8:22) · [JHN 4:4](https://ref.ly/Luke4:4) · [1CO 10:1](https://ref.ly/Rom10:1)

15\.32 · Linear Movement · Pass, Cross Over, Go Through, Go Around

to go through, to penetrate through to move through a three\-dimensional space The use of διέρχομαι in [ACT 12:10](https://ref.ly/John12:10) would suggest that the guard station was some kind of enclosure where guards stayed to control passage.

[MRK 10:25](https://ref.ly/Matt10:25) · [LUK 2:35](https://ref.ly/Mark2:35) · [ACT 12:10](https://ref.ly/John12:10) · [ROM 5:12](https://ref.ly/Acts5:12) · [HEB 4:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:14)

to feel pain and sorrow, to be sorrowful and distressed (an idiom, literally: a sword goes through one’s soul) to feel the intense pain of sorrow

[LUK 2:35](https://ref.ly/Mark2:35)

## διερωτάω (id: 001347000000000)

διερωτάω
========

διερωτάω (G1331)

ἐρωτάω

27\.11 · Learn · Learn

to learn about, to find out about by inquiry to acquire information by questioning1 Since πυνθάνομαι\[b] and διερωτάω imply quite distinct semantic components, namely ‘to acquire information’ and ‘by the process of questioning,’ it may be appropriate in many languages to use two verbs meaning ‘to ask’ and ‘to find out.’ Accordingly, this expression in [ACT 10:17](https://ref.ly/John10:17) may be rendered as ‘meanwhile, men sent by Cornelius asked and learned where Simon’s house was.’

[ACT 10:17](https://ref.ly/John10:17)

1 It is also possible to interpret διερωτάω as meaning ‘to ask questions’ or ‘to inquire about,’ in which case the meaning of διερωτάω may be treated under Domain 33 Communication.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 10:17

## διθάλασσος (id: 001353000000000)

διθάλασσος
==========

διθάλασσος (G1337)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ον 

|  |
| --- |

 δύο \+ θάλασσα 

|  |
| --- |

 ἁλίζω

14\.32 · Physical Events and States · Events Involving Liquids and Dry Masses

cross\-currents two currents which meet in a body of water Other scholars, however, interpret διθάλασσος together with τόπος as being a reef, a sandbar, or even a headland (see [1\.68](#1.68)).  
Cross\-currents may be spoken of as ‘streams in the sea’ or ‘rivers in the sea’ or ‘two rivers that meet in the sea.’ It would be wrong, however, to use the expression ‘two rivers that meet in the sea’ if this meant merely two rivers which meet at the coastline as they flow from the interior. In this context ‘rivers’ can only refer to ‘rivers of the sea,’ in other words, ‘currents.’

[ACT 27:41](https://ref.ly/John27:41)

1\.68 · Geographical Objects and Features · Land in Contrast With the Sea

**Collocation:** τόπος διθάλασσος

sandbar, reef a bar or reef produced in an area where two currents meet It is possible to understand τόπος διθάλασσος in [ACT 27:41](https://ref.ly/John27:41) as a place of crosscurrents; see [14\.32](#14.32). In some languages it may be necessary to construct a descriptive equivalent for ‘sandbank,’ for example, ‘a hill of sand just beneath the surface of the water’ or ‘a ridge of sand hidden by the water.’

[ACT 27:41](https://ref.ly/John27:41)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 27:41

21:32](https://ref.ly/Matt21:32) · [LUK 1:75](https://ref.ly/Mark1:75) · [JHN 16:8](https://ref.ly/Luke16:8) · [JHN 16:10](https://ref.ly/Luke16:10) · [ACT 10:35](https://ref.ly/John10:35) · [ACT 6:19](https://ref.ly/Acts6:19) · [ROM 6:20](https://ref.ly/Acts6:20) · [ROM 9:30](https://ref.ly/Acts9:30) · [ROM 14:17](https://ref.ly/Acts14:17) · [1CO 1:30](https://ref.ly/Rom1:30) · [2CO 11:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:15) · [EPH 4:24](https://ref.ly/Gal4:24) · [EPH 5:9](https://ref.ly/Gal5:9) · [EPH 6:14](https://ref.ly/Gal6:14) · [PHP 1:11](https://ref.ly/Eph1:11) · [PHP 3:6](https://ref.ly/Eph3:6) · [1TI 6:11](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:11) · [2TI 2:22](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:22) · [2TI 3:16](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:16) · [2TI 4:8](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:8) · [TIT 3:5](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:5) · [HEB 1:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:9) · [HEB 5:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:13) · [HEB 7:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:2) · [HEB 11:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:7) · [HEB 11:33](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:33) · [HEB 12:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:11) · [JAS 1:20](https://ref.ly/Heb1:20) · [JAS 2:23](https://ref.ly/Heb2:23) · [JAS 3:18](https://ref.ly/Heb3:18) · [1PE 2:24](https://ref.ly/Jas2:24) · [1PE 3:14](https://ref.ly/Jas3:14) · [2PE 1:1](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:1) · [2PE 2:5](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:5) · [2PE 2:21](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:21) · [2PE 3:13](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:13) · [1JN 2:29](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:29) · [1JN 3:7](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:7) · [1JN 3:10](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:10) · [REV 19:11](https://ref.ly/Jude19:11) · [REV 22:11](https://ref.ly/Jude22:11)

34\.46 · Association · Establish or Confirm a Relation

putting right with, causing to be in a right relationship with causing someone to be in a proper or right relation with someone else Some scholars, however, interpret δικαιόω, δικαίωσις, and δικαιοσύνη in the following contexts as meaning forensic righteousness, that is to say, the act of being declared righteous on the basis of Christ’s atoning ministry; but it would seem more probable that Paul uses these expressions in the context of the covenant relation rather than in the context of legal procedures.  
It may be difficult in some languages to find a succinct expression equivalent to ‘to be put right with.’ Sometimes the closest equivalent may be ‘to be related to as one should be.’ In some instances the implication of a right relationship may be expressed by phrases involving ‘acceptance.’ For example, [ROM 3:24](https://ref.ly/Acts3:24) may be expressed as ‘by the free gift of God’s grace they are accepted by him through Christ Jesus who sets them free.’ Similarly, [ROM 4:25](https://ref.ly/Acts4:25) is sometimes expressed as ‘he was raised to life in order to cause us to be accepted by God.’ There are, however, certain dangers involved in terms indicating ‘acceptance,’ since this might imply God’s reluctance to accept people apart from the atoning work of Jesus Christ, while in reality it was God who was in Christ reconciling the world to himself. Therefore, one should clearly avoid a rendering which would seem to suggest different types of motivation in the Godhead.  
Some scholars, however, understand the phrase δικαιοσύνη θεοῦ in [ROM 1:17](https://ref.ly/Acts1:17) as referring to God’s faithfulness to his promises made to Abraham. In other words, the focus would be upon God’s moral integrity, but it is difficult to relate this interpretation to the statement about faith in [ROM 1:17](https://ref.ly/Acts1:17)b.

[ROM 1:17](https://ref.ly/Acts1:17) · [ROM 3:22](https://ref.ly/Acts3:22) · [ROM 4:3](https://ref.ly/Acts4:3) · [ROM 4:5](https://ref.ly/Acts4:5) · [ROM 4:6](https://ref.ly/Acts4:6) · [ROM 4:9](https://ref.ly/Acts4:9) · [ROM 4:11](https://ref.ly/Acts4:11) · [ROM 4:11](https://ref.ly/Acts4:11) · [ROM 4:13](https://ref.ly/Acts4:13) · [ROM 4:22](https://ref.ly/Acts4:22) · [ROM 5:17](https://ref.ly/Acts5:17) · [ROM 5:21](https://ref.ly/Acts5:21) · [ROM 8:10](https://ref.ly/Acts8:10) · [ROM 9:30](https://ref.ly/Acts9:30) · [ROM 9:30](https://ref.ly/Acts9:30) · [ROM 9:31](https://ref.ly/Acts9:31) · [ROM 10:3](https://ref.ly/Acts10:3) · [ROM 10:3](https://ref.ly/Acts10:3) · [ROM 10:4](https://ref.ly/Acts10:4) · [ROM 10:5](https://ref.ly/Acts10:5) · [ROM 10:6](https://ref.ly/Acts10:6) · [ROM 10:10](https://ref.ly/Acts10:10) · [1CO 1:30](https://ref.ly/Rom1:30) · [2CO 3:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:9) · [GAL 2:21](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:21) · [GAL 3:6](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:6) · [GAL 3:21](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:21) · [GAL 5:5](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:5) · [PHP 3:9](https://ref.ly/Eph3:9) · [PHP 3:9](https://ref.ly/Eph3:9)

53\.4 · Religious Activities · Religious Practice

religious observances, religious requirements observances or practices required by one’s religion It is also possible to understand δικαιοσύνη in [MAT 6:1](https://ref.ly/Matt6:1) as meaning ‘alms’ (see [57\.111](#57.111)).

[MAT 6:1](https://ref.ly/Matt6:1)

57\.111 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

acts of charity, alms, giving to the needy giving to those in need as an act of mercy It is also possible to interpret δικαιοσύνη in [MAT 6:1](https://ref.ly/Matt6:1) as ‘religious observances’ (see [53\.4](#53.4)).

[MAT 6:1](https://ref.ly/Matt6:1)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 3:15; Matthew 5:6; Matthew 5:10; Matthew 5:20; Matthew 6:33; Matthew 21:32; Luke 1:75; John 16:8; John 16:10; Acts 10:35; Acts 13:10; Acts 17:31; Acts 24:25; Romans 3:5; Romans 3:21; Romans 3:25; Romans 3:26; Romans 6:13; Romans 6:16; Romans 6:18; Romans 6:19; Romans 6:20; Romans 9:30; Romans 14:17; 1 Corinthians 1:30; 2 Corinthians 5:21; 2 Corinthians 6:7; 2 Corinthians 6:14; 2 Corinthians 9:9; 2 Corinthians 9:10; 2 Corinthians 11:15; Ephesians 4:24; Ephesians 5:9; Ephesians 6:14; Philippians 1:11; Philippians 3:6; 1 Timothy 6:11; 2 Timothy 2:22; 2 Timothy 3:16; 2 Timothy 4:8; Titus 3:5; Hebrews 1:9; Hebrews 5:13; Hebrews 7:2; Hebrews 11:7; Hebrews 11:33; Hebrews 12:11; James 1:20; James 2:23; James 3:18; 1 Peter 2:24; 1 Peter 3:14; 2 Peter 1:1; 2 Peter 2:5; 2 Peter 2:21; 2 Peter 3:13; 1 John 2:29; 1 John 3:7; 1 John 3:10; Revelation 19:11; Revelation 22:11; Romans 1:17; Romans 3:22; Romans 4:3; Romans 4:5; Romans 4:6; Romans 4:9; Romans 4:11; Romans 4:13; Romans 4:22; Romans 5:17; Romans 5:21; Romans 8:10; Romans 9:31; Romans 10:3; Romans 10:4; Romans 10:5; Romans 10:6; Romans 10:10; 2 Corinthians 3:9; Galatians 2:21; Galatians 3:6; Galatians 3:21; Galatians 5:5; Philippians 3:9; Matthew 6:1


## δικαιόω (id: 001360000000000)

δικαιόω
=======

δικαιόω (G1344)

ἀδικέω · ἀδίκημα · ἀδικία · ἄδικος · ἀδίκως · ἀντίδικος · δικαιοκρισία · δίκαιος · δικαιοσύνη · δικαίωμα · δικαίως · δικαίωσις · δικαστής · δίκη · ἐκδικέω · ἐκδίκησις · ἔκδικος · ἔνδικος · καταδικάζω · καταδίκη · ὑπόδικος

34\.46 · Association · Establish or Confirm a Relation

to put right with, to cause to be in a right relationship with to cause someone to be in a proper or right relation with someone else Some scholars, however, interpret δικαιόω, δικαίωσις, and δικαιοσύνη in the following contexts as meaning forensic righteousness, that is to say, the act of being declared righteous on the basis of Christ’s atoning ministry; but it would seem more probable that Paul uses these expressions in the context of the covenant relation rather than in the context of legal procedures.  
It may be difficult in some languages to find a succinct expression equivalent to ‘to be put right with.’ Sometimes the closest equivalent may be ‘to be related to as one should be.’ In some instances the implication of a right relationship may be expressed by phrases involving ‘acceptance.’ For example, [ROM 3:24](https://ref.ly/Acts3:24) may be expressed as ‘by the free gift of God’s grace they are accepted by him through Christ Jesus who sets them free.’ Similarly, [ROM 4:25](https://ref.ly/Acts4:25) is sometimes expressed as ‘he was raised to life in order to cause us to be accepted by God.’ There are, however, certain dangers involved in terms indicating ‘acceptance,’ since this might imply God’s reluctance to accept people apart from the atoning work of Jesus Christ, while in reality it was God who was in Christ reconciling the world to himself. Therefore, one should clearly avoid a rendering which would seem to suggest different types of motivation in the Godhead.

[ROM 2:13](https://ref.ly/Acts2:13) · [ROM 3:20](https://ref.ly/Acts3:20) · [ROM 3:24](https://ref.ly/Acts3:24) · [ROM 3:26](https://ref.ly/Acts3:26) · [ROM 3:28](https://ref.ly/Acts3:28) · [ROM 3:30](https://ref.ly/Acts3:30) · [ROM 4:2](https://ref.ly/Acts4:2) · [ROM 4:5](https://ref.ly/Acts4:5) · [ROM 5:1](https://ref.ly/Acts5:1) · [ROM 5:9](https://ref.ly/Acts5:9) · [ROM 8:30](https://ref.ly/Acts8:30) · [ROM 8:30](https://ref.ly/Acts8:30) · [ROM 8:33](https://ref.ly/Acts8:33) · [GAL 2:16](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:16) · [GAL 2:16](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:16) · [GAL 2:16](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:16) · [GAL 2:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:17) · [GAL 3:8](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:8) · [GAL 3:11](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:11) · [GAL 3:24](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:24) · [GAL 5:4](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:4) · [TIT 3:7](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:7)

88\.16 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Just, Righteous

to show to be right, to prove to be right to demonstrate that something is morally right

[MAT 11:19](https://ref.ly/Matt11:19) · [LUK 7:35](https://ref.ly/Mark7:35) · [LUK 10:29](https://ref.ly/Mark10:29) · [LUK 16:15](https://ref.ly/Mark16:15) · [LUK 18:14](https://ref.ly/Mark18:14) · [ROM 3:4](https://ref.ly/Acts3:4) · [1TI 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:16) · [JAS 2:21](https://ref.ly/Heb2:21) · [JAS 2:24](https://ref.ly/Heb2:24) · [JAS 2:25](https://ref.ly/Heb2:25)

56\.34 · Courts and Legal Procedures · Judge, Condemn, Acquit

to acquit, to set free, to remove guilt, acquittal the act of clearing someone of transgression In a number of languages the process of acquittal takes the form of a direct statement, for example, ‘to say, You are not guilty’ or ‘..., You no longer have sin’ or, as expressed idiomatically in some instances, ‘..., Sin is no longer on your head’ or ‘..., Your sins are now given back to you.’

[MAT 12:37](https://ref.ly/Matt12:37) · [ACT 13:38](https://ref.ly/John13:38) · [ACT 13:39](https://ref.ly/John13:39) · [1CO 4:4](https://ref.ly/Rom4:4) · [1CO 6:11](https://ref.ly/Rom6:11)

37\.138 · Control, Rule · Release, Set Free

to release, to set free to cause to be released from the control of some state or situation involving moral issues In a number of languages the rendering of this expression in [ROM 6:7](https://ref.ly/Acts6:7) is extremely difficult; first, because of the figurative meaning of ‘to die to sin’ and secondly, because of the phrase ‘to be released from sin.’ It may be necessary to introduce a simile into the first clause and then to restructure considerably the second clause if one cannot speak of ‘the power of sin’ but must regard sin as exercising some kind of direct control. Accordingly, one may sometimes translate this expression in [ROM 6:7](https://ref.ly/Acts6:7) as ‘when a person is, as it were, dead as far as sinning is concerned, then sin no longer dominates him’ or ‘... then he is not controlled by his desires to sin.’

[ROM 6:7](https://ref.ly/Acts6:7)

36\.22 · Guide, Discipline, Follow · Obey, Disobey

to obey righteous commands to conform to righteous, just commands In some languages it may be difficult to translate literally ‘God’s righteous commands’ in [LUK 7:29](https://ref.ly/Mark7:29), especially since the equivalent of ‘commands’ is often a verb. Accordingly, one may need to translate ‘what God commanded, and this was right.’

[LUK 7:29](https://ref.ly/Mark7:29)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 2:13; Romans 3:20; Romans 3:24; Romans 3:26; Romans 3:28; Romans 3:30; Romans 4:2; Romans 4:5; Romans 5:1; Romans 5:9; Romans 8:30; Romans 8:33; Galatians 2:16; Galatians 2:17; Galatians 3:8; Galatians 3:11; Galatians 3:24; Galatians 5:4; Titus 3:7; Matthew 11:19; Luke 7:35; Luke 10:29; Luke 16:15; Luke 18:14; Romans 3:4; 1 Timothy 3:16; James 2:21; James 2:24; James 2:25; Matthew 12:37; Acts 13:38; Acts 13:39; 1 Corinthians 4:4; 1 Corinthians 6:11; Romans 6:7; Luke 7:29

15\.21 · Linear Movement · Travel, Journey

to travel around through, to journey all through to travel around through an area, with the implication of both extensive and thorough movement throughout an area In order to express the meaning of διοδεύω, διαπορεύομαι\[a], and διέρχομαι\[b] in these types of contexts, it may be necessary in some languages to say ‘he went from one town to another’ or, as in [ACT 13:6](https://ref.ly/John13:6), ‘he travelled to all the places on the island’ or ‘... to the various towns on the island.’

## διοπετής (id: 001372000000000)

| --- |

|  |
| --- |

2\.48 · Natural Substances · Precious and Semiprecious Stones and Substances

stone from heaven, stone fallen from the sky a stone which has fallen from heaven or the sky (originally employed in referring to images of the gods) The object referred to by τοῦ διοπετοῦς in [ACT 19:35](https://ref.ly/John19:35) was probably a stone meteorite regarded as a sacred supernatural object.

[LUK 1:13](https://ref.ly/Mark1:13) · [LUK 2:7](https://ref.ly/Mark2:7) · [LUK 21:28](https://ref.ly/Mark21:28) · [ACT 13:35](https://ref.ly/John13:35) · [ACT 18:10](https://ref.ly/John18:10) · [ACT 18:10](https://ref.ly/John18:10) · [ACT 20:26](https://ref.ly/John20:26) · [ACT 22:18](https://ref.ly/John22:18) · [ROM 1:19](https://ref.ly/Acts1:19) · [ROM 1:21](https://ref.ly/Acts1:21) · [ROM 3:20](https://ref.ly/Acts3:20) · [ROM 8:7](https://ref.ly/Acts8:7) · [1CO 15:9](https://ref.ly/Rom15:9) · [PHP 2:26](https://ref.ly/Eph2:26) · [1TH 2:8](https://ref.ly/Col2:8) · [1TH 2:18](https://ref.ly/Col2:18) · [1TH 4:6](https://ref.ly/Col4:6) · [HEB 11:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:5) · [HEB 11:23](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:23) · [JAS 4:3](https://ref.ly/Heb4:3) · [1PE 1:16](https://ref.ly/Jas1:16) · [1PE 1:24](https://ref.ly/Jas1:24) · [1PE 2:6](https://ref.ly/Jas2:6)

90\.21 · Case · Content

that, the fact that a marker of discourse content, whether direct or indirect The marking of direct and indirect discourse varies greatly from language to language. In some instances there is no marker at all; in other cases one marker precedes and another follows. In still other instances a repetition of an expression of speaking occurs at the end of a quotation, whether direct or indirect. In a number of languages written usage differs appreciably from spoken usage, because intonation so often marks introduced discourse in the spoken form of a language.  
In [ROM 8:21](https://ref.ly/Acts8:21) διότι appears to be simply a variant of ὅτι\[a], [89\.26](#89.26))

[ROM 8:20](https://ref.ly/Acts8:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:13; Luke 2:7; Luke 21:28; Acts 13:35; Acts 18:10; Acts 20:26; Acts 22:18; Romans 1:19; Romans 1:21; Romans 3:20; Romans 8:7; 1 Corinthians 15:9; Philippians 2:26; 1 Thessalonians 2:8; 1 Thessalonians 2:18; 1 Thessalonians 4:6; Hebrews 11:5; Hebrews 11:23; James 4:3; 1 Peter 1:16; 1 Peter 1:24; 1 Peter 2:6; Romans 8:20

## δίς (id: 001381000000000)

δίς
===

δίς (G1364)

adv 

|  |
| --- |

 δύο

60\.69 · Number · Once, Twice, Three Times, Etc. \[Cardinals of Time]

twice two occurrences

[MRK 14:30](https://ref.ly/Matt14:30) · [MRK 14:72](https://ref.ly/Matt14:72) · [LUK 18:12](https://ref.ly/Mark18:12) · [PHP 4:16](https://ref.ly/Eph4:16) · [1TH 2:18](https://ref.ly/Col2:18)

60\.70 · Number · Once, Twice, Three Times, Etc. \[Cardinals of Time]

**Collocation:** ἅπαξ καὶ δίς

more than once, several times (an idiom, literally: once and twice) an indefinite low number, but more than once

[PHP 4:16](https://ref.ly/Eph4:16) · [1TH 2:18](https://ref.ly/Col2:18)

23\.123 · Physiological Processes and States · Live, Die

**Collocation:** δὶς ἀποθάνων

completely dead (an idiom, literally: dying twice) the state of being completely dead The phrase δὶς ἀποθανόντα in [JUD 1:12](https://ref.ly/3John1:12) refers specifically to trees, but figuratively to persons. It is possible that δὶς ἀποθανόντα is applicable to trees (1\) on the basis that they die while still standing and (2\) that death is fully confirmed by their being rooted up, but in view of the figurative context, it is better to translate δὶς ἀποθανόντα as simply ‘completely dead.’

[JUD 1:12](https://ref.ly/3John1:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 14:30; Mark 14:72; Luke 18:12; Philippians 4:16; 1 Thessalonians 2:18; Jude 1:12


## δισμυριάς (id: 001382000000000)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-άδος 

|  |
| --- |

 δύο \+ μυρίος

60\.9 · Number · Number, Countless

countless, incalculable, great number of an indefinitely large number (even greater than μυριάς\[b], [60\.8](#60.8)) Though it is possible to understand δισμυριάδες μυριάδων in [REV 9:16](https://ref.ly/Jude9:16) as meaning ‘two hundred million’ (literally ‘twenty thousand times ten thousand’), the evident intent of the text is to emphasize the extreme number rather than to specify some large quantity.

[REV 9:16](https://ref.ly/Jude9:16)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 9:16

| --- |

 \-ας 

|  |
| --- |

 δύο \+ ἵστημι

39\.13 · Hostility, Strife · Division

division, discord a division into opposing groups, generally two In some languages the equivalent of ‘causing division’ ([ROM 16:17](https://ref.ly/Acts16:17)) is literally ‘to cause two groups in place of one group,’ but more frequently the equivalent is expressed in terms of attitudes, for example, ‘to cause people to be angry at one another’ or ‘to cause people not to like one another’ or ‘to cause people to think of one another as enemies.’

## διώκω (id: 001395000000000)

διώκω
=====

διώκω (G1377)

διωγμός · διώκτης · ἐκδιώκω · καταδιώκω

15\.158 · Linear Movement · Pursue, Follow

to run after, to chase after, to pursue to follow with haste, and presumably with intensity of effort, in order to catch up with, for friendly or hostile purpose

[MAT 23:34](https://ref.ly/Matt23:34) · [LUK 17:23](https://ref.ly/Mark17:23) · [HEB 12:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:14) · [1PE 3:11](https://ref.ly/Jas3:11) · [REV 12:13](https://ref.ly/Jude12:13)

15\.223 · Linear Movement · Goal\-Oriented Movement

to hasten, to run, to press forward, to press on to move quickly and energetically toward some objective In [PHP 3:14](https://ref.ly/Eph3:14) διώκω is to be understood in a literal sense, though the entire context is figurative. For interpreting the expression κατὰ σκοπὸν διώκω as an idiom, see [89\.56](#89.56).

[PHP 3:12](https://ref.ly/Eph3:12) · [PHP 3:14](https://ref.ly/Eph3:14)

39\.45 · Hostility, Strife · Persecution

to persecute, to harass, persecution to systematically organize a program to oppress and harass people1 In a number of languages the equivalent of ‘to persecute’ is simply ‘to cause to suffer,’ but persecution is also expressed in terms of ‘to be mean to’ or ‘to threaten’ or ‘to chase from place to place.’

## δόγμα (id: 001396000000000)

δόγμα
=====

δόγμα (G1378)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-τος 

|  |
| --- |

 δοκέω

33\.333 · Communication · Law, Regulation, Ordinance

law, ordinance, rule a formalized rule (or set of rules) prescribing what people must do The difference between ‘a law’ and ‘a command’ is that a law is enforced by sanctions from a society, while a command carries only the sanctions of the individual who commands. When, however, the people of Israel accepted the commands of God as the rules which they would follow and enforce, these became their laws.

[ACT 16:4](https://ref.ly/John16:4) · [COL 2:14](https://ref.ly/Phil2:14)

33\.332 · Communication · Command, Order

order, decree an official order or decree

[LUK 2:1](https://ref.ly/Mark2:1) · [ACT 17:7](https://ref.ly/John17:7) · [EPH 2:15](https://ref.ly/Gal2:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 16:4; Colossians 2:14; Luke 2:1; Acts 17:7; Ephesians 2:15

31\.29 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Suppose, Think Possible

to suppose, to presume, to assume, to imagine, to believe, to think to regard something as presumably true, but without particular certainty In some languages the equivalent of ‘to suppose’ or ‘to presume’ is ‘to think somewhat’ or ‘to think perhaps’ or ‘to think a little.’ In some instances the lack of certainty is spelled out clearly as ‘to think, but not with certainty’ or ‘to think, but not to know’ or ‘to think, but not to be sure.’

[MAT 6:29](https://ref.ly/Matt6:29) · [LUK 4:6](https://ref.ly/Mark4:6) · [LUK 9:26](https://ref.ly/Mark9:26) · [LUK 9:31](https://ref.ly/Mark9:31) · [LUK 9:32](https://ref.ly/Mark9:32) · [JHN 1:14](https://ref.ly/Luke1:14) · [JHN 1:14](https://ref.ly/Luke1:14) · [JHN 11:40](https://ref.ly/Luke11:40) · [JHN 12:41](https://ref.ly/Luke12:41) · [JHN 17:24](https://ref.ly/Luke17:24) · [ACT 7:2](https://ref.ly/John7:2) · [ACT 7:55](https://ref.ly/John7:55) · [ROM 1:23](https://ref.ly/Acts1:23) · [ROM 5:2](https://ref.ly/Acts5:2) · [ROM 8:18](https://ref.ly/Acts8:18) · [ROM 8:21](https://ref.ly/Acts8:21) · [1CO 2:8](https://ref.ly/Rom2:8) · [1CO 11:7](https://ref.ly/Rom11:7) · [1CO 11:7](https://ref.ly/Rom11:7) · [1CO 15:40](https://ref.ly/Rom15:40) · [1CO 15:41](https://ref.ly/Rom15:41) · [1CO 15:41](https://ref.ly/Rom15:41) · [1CO 15:41](https://ref.ly/Rom15:41) · [1CO 15:41](https://ref.ly/Rom15:41) · [1CO 15:43](https://ref.ly/Rom15:43) · [2CO 3:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:7) · [2CO 3:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:7) · [2CO 3:8](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:8) · [2CO 3:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:9) · [2CO 3:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:9) · [2CO 3:10](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:10) · [2CO 3:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:11) · [2CO 3:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:11) · [2CO 3:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:18) · [2CO 3:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:18) · [2CO 3:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:18) · [2CO 4:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:6) · [2CO 4:17](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:17) · [PHP 3:21](https://ref.ly/Eph3:21) · [COL 3:4](https://ref.ly/Phil3:4) · [2TH 1:9](https://ref.ly/1Thess1:9) · [2TH 2:14](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:14) · [2TI 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:10) · [TIT 2:13](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:13) · [HEB 1:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:3) · [HEB 2:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:7) · [HEB 2:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:9) · [HEB 9:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:5) · [JAS 2:1](https://ref.ly/Heb2:1) · [1PE 1:24](https://ref.ly/Jas1:24) · [1PE 5:4](https://ref.ly/Jas5:4) · [REV 18:1](https://ref.ly/Jude18:1) · [REV 21:23](https://ref.ly/Jude21:23)

14\.49 · Physical Events and States · Light

brightness, shining, radiance the state of brightness or shining In a number of languages a clear distinction is made between some object which is bright in and of itself (that is to say, the source of brightness or radiance) and objects which are bright because they reflect light from some source. In the case of [MAT 17:5](https://ref.ly/Matt17:5) (which is generally regarded as a reference to the Shekinah presence of God), the cloud would not be merely reflecting light but would be a source of light (see [14\.50](#14.50)).  
In [REV 15:8](https://ref.ly/Jude15:8) (καὶ ἐγεμίσθη ὁ ναὸς καπνοῦ ἐκ τῆς δόξης τοῦ θεοῦ ‘and the temple was filled with smoke from the brightness of God’) the reference is evidently to the Shekinah. The Shekinah, which filled the Temple when it was first constructed ([1KI 8:11](https://ref.ly/1Kgs8:11)), was regarded as a bright, cloud\-like object which represented the personal presence of God.

[MAT 16:27](https://ref.ly/Matt16:27) · [MAT 19:28](https://ref.ly/Matt19:28) · [MAT 25:31](https://ref.ly/Matt25:31) · [MAT 25:31](https://ref.ly/Matt25:31) · [MRK 8:38](https://ref.ly/Matt8:38) · [MRK 10:37](https://ref.ly/Matt10:37) · [LUK 2:9](https://ref.ly/Mark2:9) · [LUK 9:26](https://ref.ly/Mark9:26) · [LUK 9:31](https://ref.ly/Mark9:31) · [LUK 9:32](https://ref.ly/Mark9:32) · [LUK 24:26](https://ref.ly/Mark24:26) · [JHN 17:24](https://ref.ly/Luke17:24) · [ACT 22:11](https://ref.ly/John22:11) · [ROM 2:7](https://ref.ly/Acts2:7) · [ROM 9:23](https://ref.ly/Acts9:23) · [ROM 9:23](https://ref.ly/Acts9:23) · [1CO 15:40](https://ref.ly/Rom15:40) · [1CO 15:41](https://ref.ly/Rom15:41) · [1CO 15:41](https://ref.ly/Rom15:41) · [1CO 15:41](https://ref.ly/Rom15:41) · [1CO 15:41](https://ref.ly/Rom15:41) · [1CO 15:43](https://ref.ly/Rom15:43) · [2CO 3:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:7) · [2CO 3:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:7) · [2CO 3:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:9) · [2CO 3:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:11) · [2CO 4:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:4) · [2TH 1:9](https://ref.ly/1Thess1:9) · [HEB 1:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:3) · [HEB 9:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:5) · [REV 15:8](https://ref.ly/Jude15:8) · [REV 21:11](https://ref.ly/Jude21:11)

76\.13 · Power, Force

glorious power, amazing might a manifestation of power characterized by glory In some languages the aspect of ‘glorious’ may be expressed as ‘that which causes wonder’ or ‘that which causes people to marvel.’

[MAT 24:30](https://ref.ly/Matt24:30) · [MRK 13:26](https://ref.ly/Matt13:26) · [LUK 21:27](https://ref.ly/Mark21:27) · [ROM 6:4](https://ref.ly/Acts6:4)

33\.357 · Communication · Praise

to praise, to glorify, praise to speak of something as being unusually fine and deserving honor

12\.49 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Powers

glorious power, wonderful being a benevolent supernatural power deserving respect and honor If one can employ a phrase such as ‘wonderful beings above,’ this is fine, but in a number of languages such a phrase would refer to believers who have died. Since the reference is apparently to certain types of supernatural powers, it may be more satisfactory in some languages to speak of ‘the glorious spirits above.’

[JAS 2:1](https://ref.ly/Heb2:1) · [2PE 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:10) · [JUD 1:8](https://ref.ly/3John1:8)

1\.15 · Geographical Objects and Features · Regions Above the Earth

glory, heaven a place which is glorious and as such, a reference to heaven Some scholars, however, interpret δόξα in [1TI 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:16) as an abstract and thus translate ἐν δόξῃ as ‘in a glorious way’ or ‘in a wonderful way’ or ‘in a way that revealed his glory.’

## δουλεύω (id: 001419000000000)

δουλεύω
=======

δουλεύω (G1398)

δουλόω

87\.79 · Status · Slave, Free

to be a slave to be a slave of someone

[JHN 8:33](https://ref.ly/Luke8:33) · [ACT 7:7](https://ref.ly/John7:7) · [1TH 1:9](https://ref.ly/Col1:9)

37\.25 · Control, Rule · Control, Restrain

to be a slave to, to be controlled by (a figurative extension of meaning of δουλεύω\[a] ‘to be a slave,’ [87\.79](#87.79)) to be under the control of some influence and to serve the interests of such In a number of languages it may be difficult to translate more or less literally ‘but they serve their own appetites.’ One can, however, often translate this expression in [ROM 16:18](https://ref.ly/Acts16:18) as ‘but they do just what their own desires told them to do’ or ‘they do whatever they desired to do.’

35\.27 · Help, Care For · Serve

to serve to serve, normally in a humble manner and in response to the demands or commands of others It is possible that in [MAT 6:24](https://ref.ly/Matt6:24) δουλεύω\[a], namely, to be a slave (see [87\.79](#87.79)).

87\.83 · Status · Slave, Free

slave girl, slave woman a female slave1

[LUK 1:38](https://ref.ly/Mark1:38) · [LUK 1:48](https://ref.ly/Mark1:48) · [ACT 2:18](https://ref.ly/John2:18)

1 παιδίσκη probably refers to someone younger than would be the case for δούλη.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:38; Luke 1:48; Acts 2:18


## δοῦλος (id: 001421000000000)

δοῦλος
======

δοῦλος (G1400 · G1401)

adj 

|  |
| --- |

 \-η, \-ον

37\.3 · Control, Rule · Control, Restrain

subservient to, controlled by pertaining to a state of being completely controlled by someone or something In some languages it may be useful to render δοῦλος in the context of [ROM 6:19](https://ref.ly/Acts6:19) as a simile, ‘like slaves,’ for example, ‘for as you surrendered the parts of your body to be like slaves to obey impurity and wickedness’ or ‘... to be ordered about by impurity and wickedness.’

[ROM 6:19](https://ref.ly/Acts6:19) · [ROM 6:19](https://ref.ly/Acts6:19)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου

87\.76 · Status · Slave, Free

slave, bondservant one who is a slave in the sense of becoming the property of an owner (though in ancient times it was frequently possible for a slave to earn his freedom) When Paul speaks of himself as a slave of Jesus Christ or of God in [ROM 1:1](https://ref.ly/Acts1:1), [GAL 1:10](https://ref.ly/2Cor1:10), and [TIT 1:1](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:1), the term δοῦλος focuses attention primarily upon his belonging to Christ or to God. There are probably also important positive overtones, since in some languages of the ancient Middle East a phrase meaning ‘slave of the king’ or ‘servant of the king’ had become the title of an important person in the government. For a discussion of certain further implications of the term δοῦλος, see the discussion at [87\.81](#87.81).

[MAT 8:9](https://ref.ly/Matt8:9) · [MAT 10:24](https://ref.ly/Matt10:24) · [MAT 10:25](https://ref.ly/Matt10:25) · [MAT 13:27](https://ref.ly/Matt13:27) · [MAT 13:28](https://ref.ly/Matt13:28) · [MAT ## δουλόω (id: 001422000000000)

δουλόω
======

δουλόω (G1402) — δουλόομαι

δουλαγωγέω · δουλεία · δουλεύω · δούλη · δοῦλος · καταδουλόω · ὀφθαλμοδουλία · σύνδουλος

87\.82 · Status · Slave, Free

to enslave, to make a slave of someone to cause someone to become a slave In [ACT 7:6](https://ref.ly/John7:6) αὐτὸ refers to the preceding τὸ σπέρμα αὐτοῦ ‘his descendants.’

[ACT 7:6](https://ref.ly/John7:6) · [TIT 2:3](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:3)

37\.27 · Control, Rule · Control, Restrain

to gain control over, to make a slave of, to cause someone to be subservient to, to cause to be like a slave to gain control over someone and thus make such an individual subservient to one’s own interests

[ROM 6:18](https://ref.ly/Acts6:18) · [ROM 6:22](https://ref.ly/Acts6:22) · [1CO 7:15](https://ref.ly/Rom7:15) · [1CO 9:19](https://ref.ly/Rom9:19) · [GAL 4:3](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:3) · [2PE 2:19](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:19)

37\.24 · (δουλόομαι) · Control, Rule · Control, Restrain

to be bound, to be under obligation (a figurative extension of meaning of δουλόω\[a] ‘to enslave,’ [87\.82](#87.82)) to be firmly bound by an obligation or a relationship

[1CO 7:15](https://ref.ly/Rom7:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 7:6; Titus 2:3; Romans 6:18; Romans 6:22; 1 Corinthians 7:15; 1 Corinthians 9:19; Galatians 4:3; 2 Peter 2:19

## δράκων (id: 001424000000000)

δράκων
======

δράκων (G1404)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-οντος

4\.54 · Animals · Reptiles and Other 'Creeping Things'

dragon a legendary animal, usually regarded as being a kind of monstrous winged serpent or lizard All references to δράκων in the NT occur in the book of Revelation (chapters 12, 13, 16, and 20\), where the term is used as a descriptive epithet for the Devil. In a sense, therefore, the connotative values of the term ‘dragon’ are to some extent even more important than the specific denotation. In most areas of the world a term for dragon would imply something fearsome, but in certain parts of the Orient the dragon is regarded as the symbol of prosperity and good fortune, and it is necessary, therefore, in translating into certain languages in the Orient to employ (1\) a somewhat different expression, for example, ‘terrible reptile’ or ‘fearsome snake’ or (2\) a marginal note which will explain the differences in connotation.

[REV 12:3](https://ref.ly/Jude12:3) · [REV 12:4](https://ref.ly/Jude12:4) · [REV 12:7](https://ref.ly/Jude12:7) · [REV 12:7](https://ref.ly/Jude12:7) · [REV 12:9](https://ref.ly/Jude12:9) · [REV 12:13](https://ref.ly/Jude12:13) · [REV 12:16](https://ref.ly/Jude12:16) · [REV 12:17](https://ref.ly/Jude12:17) · [REV 13:2](https://ref.ly/Jude13:2) · [REV 13:4](https://ref.ly/Jude13:4) · [REV 13:11](https://ref.ly/Jude13:11) · [REV 16:13](https://ref.ly/Jude16:13) · [REV 20:2](https://ref.ly/Jude20:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 12:3; Revelation 12:4; Revelation 12:7; Revelation 12:9; Revelation 12:13; Revelation 12:16; Revelation 12:17; Revelation 13:2; Revelation 13:4; Revelation 13:11; Revelation 16:13; Revelation 20:2

## δρέπανον (id: 001427000000000)

δρέπανον
========

δρέπανον (G1407)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου

6\.5 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Agriculture and Husbandry

sickle a large, curved knife employed in cutting ripe grain or grapes Where there is no receptor language term for sickle, one may often employ a descriptive phrase such as ‘a knife for harvesting grain’ or ‘a curved knife for cutting grain.’

[MRK 4:29](https://ref.ly/Matt4:29) · [REV 14:14](https://ref.ly/Jude14:14) · [REV 14:15](https://ref.ly/Jude14:15) · [REV 14:16](https://ref.ly/Jude14:16) · [REV 14:17](https://ref.ly/Jude14:17) · [REV 14:18](https://ref.ly/Jude14:18) · [REV 14:18](https://ref.ly/Jude14:18) · [REV 14:19](https://ref.ly/Jude14:19)

43\.17 · Agriculture

**Collocation:** βάλλω τὸ δρέπανον

to use a sickle, to swing a sickle, to begin to harvest (an idiom, literally: to throw a sickle) to begin to harvest a crop by cutting ripe grain with a sickle In [REV 14:16](https://ref.ly/Jude14:16) and [REV 14:19](https://ref.ly/Jude14:19) this idiom occurs in a figurative context, and therefore it may be necessary in some languages to speak of ‘harvesting’ rather than using a phrase which mentions the literal use of a sickle.

[REV 14:16](https://ref.ly/Jude14:16) · [REV 14:19](https://ref.ly/Jude14:19)

43\.17 · Agriculture

**Collocation:** ἀποστέλλω τὸ δρέπανον · πέμπω τὸ δρέπανον

to use a sickle, to swing a sickle, to begin to harvest (idioms, literally: to send a sickle) to begin to harvest a crop by cutting ripe grain with a sickle In [REV 14:15](https://ref.ly/Jude14:15) and [REV 14:18](https://ref.ly/Jude14:18) this idiom occurs in a figurative context, and therefore it may be necessary in some languages to speak of ‘harvesting’ rather than using a phrase which mentions the literal use of a sickle.

[MRK 4:29](https://ref.ly/Matt4:29) · [REV 14:15](https://ref.ly/Jude14:15) · [REV 14:18](https://ref.ly/Jude14:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 4:29; Revelation 14:14; Revelation 14:15; Revelation 14:16; Revelation 14:17; Revelation 14:18; Revelation 14:19

## δύναμις (id: 001431000000000)

δύναμις
=======

δύναμις (G1411)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-εως 

|  |
| --- |

 δύναμαι

74\.1 · Able, Capable

ability, capability the ability to perform a particular activity or to undergo some experience In a number of languages the equivalent of ‘ability’ in [2CO 1:8](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:8) may be expressed simply by a modal such as ‘can,’ for example, ‘far beyond what we can endure.’

[MAT 25:15](https://ref.ly/Matt25:15) · [1CO 4:19](https://ref.ly/Rom4:19) · [2CO 1:8](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:8) · [2CO 8:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:3) · [2CO 8:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:3) · [HEB 11:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:11)

76\.1 · Power, Force

power the potentiality to exert force in performing some function

76\.7 · Power, Force

mighty deed, miracle a deed manifesting great power, with the implication of some supernatural force

[MAT 7:22](https://ref.ly/Matt7:22) · [MAT 11:20](https://ref.ly/Matt11:20) · [MAT 11:21](https://ref.ly/Matt11:21) · [MAT 11:23](https://ref.ly/Matt11:23) · [MAT 13:54](https://ref.ly/Matt13:54) · [MAT 13:58](https://ref.ly/Matt13:58) · [MAT 14:2](https://ref.ly/Matt14:2) · [MRK 6:2](https://ref.ly/Matt6:2) · [MRK 6:5](https://ref.ly/Matt6:5) · [MRK 6:14](https://ref.ly/Matt6:14) · [MRK 9:39](https://ref.ly/Matt9:39) · [LUK 10:13](https://ref.ly/Mark10:13) · [LUK 19:37](https://ref.ly/Mark19:37) · [ACT 2:22](https://ref.ly/John2:22) · [ACT 8:13](https://ref.ly/John8:13) · [ACT 19:11](https://ref.ly/John19:11) · [1CO 12:10](https://ref.ly/Rom12:10) · [1CO 12:28](https://ref.ly/Rom12:28) · [1CO 12:29](https://ref.ly/Rom12:29) · [2CO 12:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:12) · [GAL 3:5](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:5) · [PHP 3:10](https://ref.ly/Eph3:10) · [1TH 1:5](https://ref.ly/Col1:5) · [2TH 2:9](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:9) · [HEB 2:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:4)

37\.61 · Control, Rule · Rule, Govern

ruler one who has the power to rule It is also possible to interpret δύναμις in [ROM 8:38](https://ref.ly/Acts8:38) as meaning a supernatural power (see [12\.44](#12.44)).

[ROM 8:38](https://ref.ly/Acts8:38) · [1CO 15:24](https://ref.ly/Rom15:24)

12\.44 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Powers

power, authority, lordship, ruler, wicked force (title for supernatural forces and powers) a supernatural power having some particular role in controlling the destiny and activities of human beings Some scholars have believed that it is possible to reconstruct at least in part some of the hierarchy represented by these various supernatural forces and powers, on the basis of the neoplatonic system of nine such powers arranged in three orders of three each. NT terminology and usage does not, however, lend itself to such a classification, and it is difficult, if not impossible, to determine what are the significant differences between these supernatural powers and forces.  
In the case of [EPH 1:21](https://ref.ly/Gal1:21) some scholars apply the terms in question both to the supernatural and to the human sphere, thus emphasizing the totality of Christ’s rule. This has a considerable measure of justification in view of the concepts held by persons in the ancient world, since various earthly powers were supposed to reflect corresponding supernatural powers.  
For the most part, translators have endeavored to render the various terms in somewhat different ways, for example, ἐξουσία as ‘authority’; δύναμις as ‘power’; κυριότης as ‘ruler’; and phrases such as τὰ πνευματικὰ τῆς πονηρίας ἐν τοῖς ἐπουρανίοις as ‘wicked spiritual forces in the heavenly world.’ In a number of languages, however, there are simply not enough terms to designate various kinds of powers, authorities, and forces which could be employed in speaking of such supernatural impersonal powers. Accordingly, some translators have simply used a phrase such as ‘any and all kinds of supernatural powers.’ Where it is possible to make certain lexical distinctions between terms and phrases, this, of course, should be done, but in a number of contexts this may be impossible, and accordingly, some explanation in a marginal note may be required if the reader is to understand satisfactorily the intent of the passages in question.

[MAT 24:29](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29) · [MAT 26:64](https://ref.ly/Matt26:64) · [MRK 13:25](https://ref.ly/Matt13:25) · [MRK 14:62](https://ref.ly/Matt14:62) · [LUK 21:26](https://ref.ly/Mark21:26) · [ACT 8:10](https://ref.ly/John8:10) · [ROM 8:38](https://ref.ly/Acts8:38) · [1CO 15:24](https://ref.ly/Rom15:24) · [EPH 1:21](https://ref.ly/Gal1:21) · [1PE 3:22](https://ref.ly/Jas3:22)

33\.134 · Communication · Interpret, Mean, Explain

meaning, what is intended the meaning or significance of a word or statement It is, of course, also possible to translate [1CO 14:11](https://ref.ly/Rom14:11) as ‘if I cannot understand what has been said.’

[1CO 14:11](https://ref.ly/Rom14:11)

## δυνάστης (id: 001433000000000)

δυνάστης
========

δυνάστης (G1413)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 δύναμαι

37\.62 · Control, Rule · Rule, Govern

official, ruler (derivative of δύναμις\[d] ‘ruler,’ [37\.61](#37.61)) one who is in a position of authority to command others

[LUK 1:52](https://ref.ly/Mark1:52) · [ACT 8:27](https://ref.ly/John8:27)1 · [1TI 6:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:15)

1 ACT 8:27 In [ACT 8:27](https://ref.ly/John8:27) δυνάστης reinforces the meaning of εὐνοῦχος in the sense of ‘court official’ (see [37\.85](#37.85)).

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:52; Acts 8:27; 1 Timothy 6:15

adj

60\.11 · Number · One, Two, Three, Etc. \[Cardinals]

two cardinal number, where there are two instances of a countable entity In a number of languages it is not possible to use numbers as pronominal substitutes for specific references to animate or inanimate objects. ## δύσις (id: 001441000000000)

δύσις
=====

δύσις (G1424a)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-εως 

|  |
| --- |

 δύνω

82\.2 · Spacial Orientations · North, South, East, West

west west (as the direction of the setting sun) In most languages east and west are related to the rising or setting sun, although in some languages there may be some local geographical feature which serves as a marker of direction, for example, the location of a particular mountain, the ocean, or a river. For north, some languages employ ‘to the left of the rising sun,’ that is to say, the direction is oriented in terms of the left hand of a person facing toward the rising sun. Similarly, south would be ‘to the right of the rising sun.’

[MRK 16:8](https://ref.ly/Matt16:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 16:8

## δυσκόλως (id: 001443000000000)

δυσκόλως
========

δυσκόλως (G1423)

adv 

|  |
| --- |

 δῦσ\- \+ κωλύω

22\.32 · Trouble, Hardship, Relief, Favorable Circumstances · Difficult, Hard

difficult, hard, with difficulty pertaining to that which is difficult to accomplish or do In some languages it may be difficult to render concisely the expression ‘only with difficulty.’ To express this contrastive element in connection with entering the kingdom of heaven, one must often translate as ‘a rich person will be able to enter into the kingdom of heaven, but it will be very difficult for him to do so.’

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 19:23; Mark 10:23; Luke 18:24

## δῶμα (id: 001451000000000)

δῶμα
====

δῶμα (G1430)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-τος 

|  |
| --- |

 ἐνδώμησις · ἐποικοδομέω · οἰκοδομέω · οἰκοδομή · οἰκοδόμος · συνοικοδομέω

7\.51 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

housetop the area on the top of a flat\-roof house The phrase κηρύξατε ἐπὶ τῶν δωμάτων ‘proclaim from the housetops’ ([MAT 10:27](https://ref.ly/Matt10:27)) is an idiom meaning ‘to proclaim publicly’ (see [28\.64](#28.64)). See [7\.50](#7.50) for comments relating to translational problems.

[MAT 10:27](https://ref.ly/Matt10:27) · [MAT 24:17](https://ref.ly/Matt24:17) · [MRK 13:15](https://ref.ly/Matt13:15) · [LUK 5:19](https://ref.ly/Mark5:19) · [LUK 12:3](https://ref.ly/Mark12:3) · [LUK 17:31](https://ref.ly/Mark17:31) · [ACT 10:9](https://ref.ly/John10:9)

28\.64 · Know · Able To Be Known

**Collocation:** ἐπὶ τῶν δωμάτων

in public, publicly (an idiom, literally: on the housetops) pertaining to being widely known in view of the events in question having taken place in public1

[MAT 10:27](https://ref.ly/Matt10:27) · [LUK 12:3](https://ref.ly/Mark12:3)

1 It is very possible that the two idioms in [28\.64](#28.64) differ somewhat in meaning, or at least in connotation, but it is difficult, if not impossible, to show this from existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 10:27; Matthew 24:17; Mark 13:15; Luke 5:19; Luke 12:3; Luke 17:31; Acts 10:9

## δῶρον (id: 001456000000000)

δῶρον
=====

δῶρον (G1435)

noun 

|  |
| --- |

 \-ου 

|  |
| --- |

 δωρέομαι

57\.84 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

gift, present (derivative of δωρέομαι ‘to give, to grant,’ [57\.83](#57.83)) that which is given or granted Since δῶρον in [MAT 5:24](https://ref.ly/Matt5:24) refers specifically to the sacrifice, it may be useful to translate this phrase as ‘leave there your sacrifice before the altar.’

[MAT 2:11](https://ref.ly/Matt2:11) · [MAT 5:23](https://ref.ly/Matt5:23) · [MAT 5:24](https://ref.ly/Matt5:24) · [MAT 5:24](https://ref.ly/Matt5:24) · [MAT 8:4](https://ref.ly/Matt8:4) · [MAT 15:5](https://ref.ly/Matt15:5) · [MAT 23:18](https://ref.ly/Matt23:18) · [MAT 23:19](https://ref.ly/Matt23:19) · [MAT 23:19](https://ref.ly/Matt23:19) · [MRK 7:11](https://ref.ly/Matt7:11) · [LUK 21:1](https://ref.ly/Mark21:1) · [LUK 21:4](https://ref.ly/Mark21:4) · [EPH 2:8](https://ref.ly/Gal2:8) · [HEB 5:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:1) · [HEB 8:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:3) · [HEB 8:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:4) · [HEB 9:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:9) · [HEB 11:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:4) · [REV 11:10](https://ref.ly/Jude11:10)

6\.142 · Artifacts · Containers

offering box a place for making gifts or offerings (see γαζοφυλάκιον\[b] \- [6\.141](#6.141)) According to tradition there were thirteen such offering boxes in the Temple and the receptacles leading down to the boxes were made in the form of trumpets. As a result, the sound of coins falling into the boxes was rather conspicuous.  
In [LUK 21:4](https://ref.ly/Mark21:4) it is possible to interpret εἰς τὰ δῶρα not as ‘into the offering boxes’ but as ‘for their gifts,’ thus reflecting a more common meaning of δῶρον\[a] gift ([57\.84](#57.84)).

[LUK 21:4](https://ref.ly/Mark21:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 2:11; Matthew 5:23; Matthew 5:24; Matthew 8:4; Matthew 15:5; Matthew 23:18; Matthew 23:19; Mark 7:11; Luke 21:1; Luke 21:4; Ephesians 2:8; Hebrews 5:1; Hebrews 8:3; Hebrews 8:4; Hebrews 9:9; Hebrews 11:4; Revelation 11:10

noun

| --- |

| --- |

 δωρέομαι \+ φέρω

57\.86 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

bringing of gifts the bringing of a gift or present This word is found as a variant reading only: ἡ δωροφορία μου ἡ εἰς Ἰερουσαλὴμ εὐπρόσδεκτος τοῖς ἁγίοις γένηται ‘that my bringing of gifts to Jerusalem may be acceptable to God’s people (there)’ [ROM 15:31](https://ref.ly/Acts15:31) (apparatus).

[ROM 15:31](https://ref.ly/Acts15:31)
